![480805835_122228208596031351_2828057899386139952_n.jpg](Chapter%2022%20-%20Ferron/480805835_122228208596031351_2828057899386139952_n.jpg)

The noise was unbearable.

The battle cries. The agonizing screams. The crunch of metal. The clanking of swords against shields and plates. The firing and exploding of artillery. The guttural cries of Rhonza warriors dying for causes that Haoyu and Dallas didn’t even begin to understand.

“Jesus Christ…” Haoyu whispered, gripping the edge of the tower wall.

Dallas was speechless. Eyes wide. Jaw tight.

Haoyu leaned over the edge.

His breath caught.

Eyes widened.

Jaw slackened.

And something inside him ; deep in his spine ; shivered.

Dallas noticed.

“You alright, partner? All this war is too much ain’t it?” he asked, edging closer.

Haoyu didn’t answer.

He just raised a trembling hand… and pointed.

Dallas followed his gaze.

And froze.

There, at the center of the battlefield, in the blood-slicked heart of the chaos, stood something that did not belong.

Not a Rhonza. Not an Oc’Xari. Not a human.

Not anything of this world.

It stood atop a pile of broken bodies ; as if it had emerged from the carnage, birthed from slaughter.

A towering flesh-beast, its skin bloated and pus-slicked, bulging in places like it was filled with rotting gas. It stood on three legs, crooked and unnaturally jointed, with two massive arms, long enough to drag against the ground ; the hands a fusion of hoof and claw.

Its head was unmistakably in the shape of a **pig.**

Tusks curled forward from a snouted mouth that did not breathe ; and horns jutted from its scalp, not symmetrical, not organic, but warped like melted iron.

Its eyes ; if you could call them that ; were holes, black and bottomless, fixed directly on Haoyu and Dallas.

It wasn’t thrashing. It wasn’t rampaging.

It was still and silent, like a statue, from over 100 meters away, watching Haoyu and Dallas.

“No...” Haoyu muttered, voice shaking. “No, that’s impossible.”

Dallas stepped back, instinctively clutching his chest ; as if the thing had already reached it’s presence inside him.

He swallowed hard.

“That’s the Pig I saw… back in the saloon on Nhexus…”

Dallas backed toward the wall of the tower, eyes locked to the pit.

“It’s looking right at us.”

The beast didn’t move.

**But suddenly Everything else… stopped.**

The chaos of war ; the clashing of steel, the cries of pain, the roar of catapults ; halted.

Rhonza soldiers froze mid-strike, blades locked in the air.

Smoke stopped rising.

Embers stopped flickering.

The wind stopped blowing.

The entire battlefield went dead ; like someone had pressed pause on reality.

Only the Pig remained animate.

Still staring.

Still watching.

Dallas didn’t breathe. Neither did Haoyu.

And then

The voice came.

It didn’t echo.

It didn’t vibrate through air.

It pounded through their bones.

A voice so low, so thunderous, it felt like it came from beneath the world, dragging fire and ash in its wake.

"You do not belong here mortal."

The sky above them darkened unnaturally.

A pressure fell on their chests, like invisible chains.

"You chase stars and scratch at doors that were never meant to open."

The Pig still hadn’t moved.

But the voice… was coming from it.

Through it.

Or from something inside it.

"You mortals are meddling in business beyond your comprehension."

"You scoured Nhexus. You opened the gates. Now the door opens both ways."

Haoyu's knees buckled. He hit the floor of the tower with a thud.

Dallas stumbled back, one hand gripping the railing, his knuckles white.

"You prod the bones of what came before the first spark."

"There are forces older than light."

"Older than the seed of life. Older than the silence that birthed the stars."

A pause.

Then, colder, quieter, somehow closer:

"You have seen far too much for the mortal eye."

A pause.

A tremor in the sky.

And then

With rage that could split worlds, the voice snarled:

"Now… **GET OUT OF MY REALM**."

![485975375_122234750132031351_5303640472531698271_n.jpg](Chapter%2022%20-%20Ferron/485975375_122234750132031351_5303640472531698271_n.jpg)

---

### IV. Swift Current Ranch - 4:21 AM

Haoyu jerked awake, gasping for breath.

His chest heaved like he’d just been pulled from a freezing lake.

His shirt clung to his skin, drenched in sweat. Beside him, his wife stirred groggily, murmuring his name in concern ; but he couldn’t speak yet.

He sat upright on the makeshift bedroll, heart pounding.

The smell of hay. Wood. A sliver of moonlight through the window. The real world.

But it didn’t feel real.

Across the room, just outside the faint glow of the nightlight… someone was watching him.

Dmitry.

Seated in the kitchen chair, facing him silently. Still. Pale.

His tablet; covered in analog sensors, antennae, and etched coil rings ; hummed quietly in his lap, lit with dozens of warning glyphs.

Haoyu blinked, trying to get words out.

Dmitry stood slowly.

“You were gone for a while,” he said, voice hushed and flat.


“Two hours. Maybe more.”

Haoyu’s throat was dry.

“...Gone?” he croaked.

Dmitry didn’t blink.

“There was something standing over you the whole time. Shadow... thin. Elongated. Same morphology we saw on Nhexus in the crater footage from Echofall Day 76.”

Haoyu stared at him.

Dmitry continued:

“It never moved. It just… touched your head. Watched you.”
” I sat down on this chair, and it glanced at me- started watching me.”


“I watched it back.”

“We didn’t speak. And there was no aggression, just watching each other.”

He stepped slightly closer, lowering his voice:

“At one point, you were squirming, and it looked at me, and it looked like it was touching it’s temple, and trying to communicate something to me - it didn’t seem evil in it’s intent, seemed like it was trying to show you something.”

Haoyu rubbed his face, trembling.

“I saw it.”

Dmitry tilted his head.

“What did you see?”

Haoyu nodded, then exhaled shakily.

“I was on this planet called Ferron. A whole world of iron and flame. There was a battle. Massive. Ancient. Terrifying.”

He paused.

Then, voice low and rattled:

“And in the middle of it all… I saw it again. The same pig-like thing from another dream I have back on Nhexus. But instead of in the Saloon, the Pig was standing on a mound of corpses. It didn’t fight. Didn’t move. Just… watched us.”

Dmitry remained still.

“Did it do anything?”

“Yeah, it spoke to us this time” Haoyu whispered.

He looked down, breath shallow.

“It told us we’d seen too much. That the map… wasn’t meant for us. That something older than life itself was watching now. And then it screamed; told us to get out.”

Dmitry slowly sat back down.

“They’ve followed us through the data. Through the probe. Through the signal. Now… through the dreams.”

He looked out the window at the prairie moonlight.

“Echofall wasn’t just a project.”

“It opened a door to another world, and now it’s left wide open.”

Haoyu’s voice trailed off.

He sat still for a long moment, trying to hold onto the last flickers of that infernal battlefield ; the warmth of the forge winds, the piercing silence that followed the beast’s command.

Dmitry stood slowly, the faint chime of his device now rising in pitch ; the interface blinking with overlapping coordinate arcs and waveforms, displayed in holographic pulses across the cracked screen.

He tapped the side of it, pulled up the map.

And there it was.

A line.

A glowing trajectory slashing through the simulated cosmos of known and hypothesized systems ; originating somewhere just beyond Ferron’s modeled cluster. The endpoint?

A bright coordinate blip hovering in Haoyu’s region of the bed.

Dmitry turned the screen toward him.

“The moment you entered REM,” he said, voice steady, “this device began capturing... a transmission.”


“Not radio. Not subspace. Something deeper. Something laced into particle resonance.”

He paused, then clarified:

“Your mind ; your body ; was generating an emission.”


“The map registered it. The same kind of pulse signature as the Oc’Xari guitar when we analyzed it yesterday.”

“But this time… there was a destination ping.”

He tapped the glowing node.

“Ferron. Not metaphorically. Not in dream logic. Literally, physically, cosmologically real. Your consciousness made contact with a fixed location in space.”

Haoyu blinked.

“We... projected?”

Dmitry nodded once.

“Like quantum resonance through folded memory-space. Your brain is being used like a tuning fork ; like an anchor. Something out there is pulling you in, using the guitar’s signature as a conduit.”

He flicked to another screen ; jagged spikes of frequency activity.

“You weren’t imagining the battlefield. Or the Pig-Beast. Or the city.”


“Those places exist.”

“And Oc’Xari entity ; is bringing you there, like its trying to show you something.”

He looked back up, face pale but unwavering.

“These aren’t dreams, Commander.”


“They’re transits.”

Haoyu’s stomach sank.

“So when it said we weren’t supposed to be there…”

Dmitry’s expression tightened grimly.

“It meant it. Whatever this is ; it’s more ancient than Oc’Xari, more dangerous than anything Echofall imagined. You’ve been seen, Haoyu.”

He looked toward the hallway.

“And if it’s watching us in our own sleep…”


“…it’s already here.”

---

[Chapter 23 - The Donkey](Chapter%2023%20-%20The%20Donkey%201ebfda674d69809db6d3ef1cdb2ba1d4.md)

---

# Chapter 23 - The Donkey

---

### I. **Day 2 & 3: The Lab, The Ranch, The Raid and The Mystical Six Legged Donkey**

The morning after the Ferron dream, the crew gathered in the barn around Dmitry’s tablet -reviewing everything.

Frequency patterns. Energy waves. Gravitational bleed.

Dmitry’s voice was calm but firm as he ran them through it all:

“This wasn’t just a dream. There were emissions. Echoes in the Schumann resonance bands. I charted it. We can triangulate the entrypoint.”

Haoyu rubbed his temple, exhausted and electrified all at once.

“So this… Ferron… was real. We were there.”

Dmitry didn’t answer. He just tapped the map ; a faint glowing line drawn from Earth to a coordinate far outside the Kuiper Belt.

---

By 10:00 AM, the crew had split up into work roles.

Steven took the rental car, heading into Swift Current for bulk gear ; monitors, folding tables, ethernet spools, surge batteries, and whatever sleeping gear the local stores had.

Yuyan took Dallas’ F1 truck, cruising slow and steady down the dusty roads with a shopping list of his own ; conduit wire, microwave components, copper spools, and antenna tubing. He said he could probably make a satellite uplink “if given some foil and enough faith.”

Dallas handed him some gas money and pointed him to the old supply road into town.

“Try not to get pulled over. Pretty sure that truck’s got 1949 plates.” Dallas remarked.


 “But she sings.” Yuyan replied.

---

The rest of the day was spent building.

The barn filled with the sound of drills, bolt-tighteners, and the occasional "ow!" from Steven when he dropped a battery on his foot.

Desks were rigged up. A generator wired to solar input.

By sundown, the workspace felt like a command center.

Evening came. Dinner was quiet, filled with subdued jokes and tired glances.

The stars twinkled over the prairie sky.

No dreams that night.

---

Day 3 came peacefully.

The kids ran around the farmhouse, sword-fighting with twigs, shrieking with laughter.

Dallas handed out chore duties with a half-serious smirk.

“If y’all are settin’ up shop here, you’re gonna earn your keep.”

Pragnya mucked out the goat pen.

Dmitry helped replace a fence panel.

Steven rode a tractor for the first time in his life and absolutely loved it.

Haoyu stood on the porch beside his wife, arm draped around her shoulders, watching it all unfold.

“It’s not much,” he said.


“It’s everything,” she replied.

Dinner that night was beans, bread, and quiet contentment.

Another night passed.

Another peaceful, dreamless night.

---

### II. Detainment

**Day 4** - 5:03 AM.

The sun hadn’t yet crested over the frost-tipped fields. The barn lights were off. The wind was still.

Until the pounding came.

Loud. Repetitive. Unrelenting.

BANG. BANG. BANG.

“Open the door! POLICE! OPEN UP!”

Children screamed.

Dallas was already halfway down the stairs, hair a mess, reaching to open the front door.

“Hold on! What in god’s-”

The door exploded inward, smashing into Dallas’s chest like a battering ram. It launched him across the kitchen, sending him sprawling over a stool and shattering the coffee table.

**Flashbang**.

A white-hot burst of light and sound detonated in the center of the living room, rattling the very bones of the house.

Haoyu dove instinctively to shield his children, but it was too late ; the shockwave flooded everything. His ears rang like artillery. Vision fractured into afterimages. His kids shrieked in confusion.

“Get on the floor! Hands where we can see them!”

Heavy boots thundered in. Muffled radio commands. Lasers sweeping across every surface. Automatic rifles raised. Every movement barked at. Every voice drowned in chaos.

Before Haoyu could utter a word, he was wrenched to the floor, arm twisted behind his back, metal clicking into place around his wrists.

“Commander Zhang, you’re under federal detainment pending investigation of interstellar trafficking, fraudulent claims unauthorized alien contact, failing to appear in the court of law, and obstruction of classified research property.”

“You have no jurisdiction here!” Dmitry shouted somewhere across the room.

A rifle slammed into his spine. The primary CIA officer pulls out a scroll reading; Certification of Approved Investigation by the Government of Canada

“We do now, bitch.”

---

The barn lab ; still half-finished, computers all over the place, half loaded into server racks, cables still exposed, coffee cups still half full from the night before; was immediately surrounded.

Agents in black paramilitary suits stormed the threshold, sweeping with sensors, placing seizure tags on:

- The alien guitar, carefully unwrapped and zipped into a triple-sealed biohazard box.
- All laptops, antennae, and monitoring relays
- Even the custom chairs Yuyan and Steven had spent all day building from scrap

Inside the garage, the 1950 Ford F1 - shining like a dream from another century - was marked “PROPERTY OF JAMES BETHOZ // INTERDIMENSIONAL ASSET TRACKING.”

The plate was removed.

The keys, confiscated.

---

The entire crew ; Haoyu, Dmitry, Pragnya, Steven, Yuyan ; were marched out individually, still in their pajamas or half-dressed, blinking under the glare of helicopter lights and drone cameras circling overhead. 

Dallas - barely conscious and probably had a few ribs broken - hauled off into a separate police truck

Haoyu’s wife clutched their kids close, crying, screaming at the soldiers.

“He didn’t do anything! He’s a scientist! Our kids; our kids are terrified!”

They were separated.

The children were led into a white unmarked car. His wife, tear-streaked and trembling, shoved into the passenger seat of a different cruiser, fighting to keep her eyes on Haoyu.

“Don’t let them take you,” she sobbed. “Don’t you disappear on us.”

Haoyu was thrown into the back of an armored transport, his face pressed against the cold metal bars.

The drive to the facility felt like it took forever.

---

### **III. Processing**

Each crew member was placed in a separate, isolated holding cell ; no communication. No contact.

Bright white lights. Metal benches. Walls so sterile they hurt the eyes.

Interrogations began one by one.

---

**Ex Commander Haoyu Zhang - Former Lead of Project Echofall**

He was left in the room for nearly an hour.

No clock.

No sound.

Just the soft hum of fluorescent light and the faint static crackle from the observation glass.

When the door finally opened, two men in black suits entered ; crisp, cold, zero insignia. Not even nametags. One carried a tablet. The other, a steel briefcase he never opened.

They sat across from him. No greeting. No handshake.

Just the questions.

Agent:

“Commander. Why did you run from court?”

Haoyu exhaled slowly.

“I had leads to uncover mysteries beyond what humanity has ever encountered, I was chosen, we don’t even know why! We could reopen the project and bring more evidence to my case in my defence!”

Agent:

“Why did you take a team of laid-off government scientists to a different country to follow an alien signal?”

Haoyu:

“Because I’ve spent half my life chasing signals from a dead planet. And when one of those signals points at your dreams, your house, your wife ; you follow it.”

Agent:

“Where did you get the truck?”

Haoyu:

(Dry laugh)


“I have no idea how it got here. I don’t even know how to drive it properly.”

Agent:

“Where did the guitar come from?”

Haoyu:

“Dallas said an Oc’Xari just showed up and gave it to him.”

Agent:

“What is the function of the forge-world you referenced in your notes?”

Haoyu leaned forward.

Eyes sharp.

“It’s not a simulation. It’s not just a world. Ferron is a real place ; a whole planet ; we were *placed* on it, through some astral projection energy.”


“These aren’t hallucinations. They’re interdimensional correspondence. It’s like remoting into a computer*.*”

Agent:

“Who, or what- is the Pig Entity?”

Haoyu's voice faltered for the first time.

A pause.

“...I don’t know.”


“I don’t have evidence yet, but I don’t think it’s from Ferron or Nhexus, and it’s not an Oc’Xari.”

Agent:

“Is it a weapon?”

Haoyu:

“I have no idea what it is.”

Agent:

“Are you a threat?”

Haoyu met their eyes. Calm now.

“no, of course not.”


“The Echofall probe didn’t just find life. It woke something up. And now, you’re asking me if I’m the threat? I’m trying to figure it out!”

---

**Dmitry Alexeyev - Lead Systems Engineer, Russian immigrant**

Agent:

“You were on the original Echofall design committee, correct? The backbone of the signal intelligence platform?”

Dmitry: *(grunts, cold and unimpressed)*

“Ya. I built the backbone. Fed it iron and fire for twenty years while your politicians cut its legs off with red tape and cowardice.”

Agent:

“And you’re claiming the dreams emit quantifiable signals?”

Dmitry: *(leans in, knuckles cracked, voice rough as rusted steel)*

“You listen now. I fought in the Kholm Petrovski battle in Siberia when I was seventeen. Then I built battlefield comms for five governments across three wars. I don’t ‘claim.’ I measure. I log. I triangulate. I have monitoring tools that record actual, repeatable, mathematical data ; measurable waveform bursts, localized field anomalies, synchronized cerebral pulse events.”

Agent:

“What about the entity you claimed to observe in the room?”

Dmitry: *(snorts with fury)*

“Not ‘claimed,’ you imperial idiot. We photographed that shadow thing with the Echofall rover on Nhexus thirteen years ago. We have hard data, real footage, logs signed by your own military subcontractors. I sat three hours watching it stare into the rovers camera. Meanwhile, your analysts were jerking off in fancy offices, not doing shit!”

Agent:

“You could’ve reported it”

Dmitry: *(cuts him off, ice in his tone)*

“I did. Forty-seven times. Every time? Buried. Redacted. Reassigned. You can probably check your fucking emails and find my submissions.”

---

**Pragnya Reddy - The Systems Engineer and Biologist** sat with arms crossed, still wearing the same hoodie from the farm ; dark circles under her eyes, but spine straight. She didn’t flinch when the agents walked in.

Agent:


“You’re the one who re-validated the genome sequencing on the Nhexus samples?”

Pragnya:


“Three times. Independently. In two separate labs. Every nucleotide pattern matched LUCA identifiers within 0.003% variance.”

Agent:


“So you’re claiming life on Earth and life on Nhexus share a common ancestor?”

Pragnya:


“No. I’m proving it.”

Agent:


“You think that justifies violating international data sovereignty and collaborating with fugitives?”

Pragnya: (shrugs)


“I followed the data. It didn’t stop at borders.”

Agent:


“And the guitar? The dreams?”

Pragnya:


“We don’t have the answers to that- we are trying to discover what they mean.”

---

**Steven Young - The Swamp Redneck**, still in shorts and his ridiculous cowboy hat, just smirked through half the interview.

“I told you folks I just came to help build a lab. Y’all didn’t say there’d be no moonshine and only jail time.”

Agent:

“You flew from Florida to rural Saskatchewan to build a lab around an alien guitar?”

Steven: *(grinning like he’s about to sell a used tractor)*

“Well I didn’t come for the weather, that’s for damn sure. Cold up here like a gator’s ass in a snowstorm. But yeah, Dallas called. Said there was a magic guitar and possible interdimensional bullshittery, so I packed my boots and scanners and hopped on a plane.”

Agent:

“Bullshittery isn’t a scientific term.”

Steven: *(shrugs)*

“Ain’t got time for textbooks when the dream gods are flingin’ folks across space-time. I saw that map glow like a bass tracker sonar on meth. Whatever’s in that wood? It ain’t human.”

Agent:

“You understood the risks of harboring a possibly illegal extraterrestrial object?”

Steven: *(snorts)*

“Buddy, I once duct-taped a live possum to a lightning rod just to measure atmospheric ion surges. You think I care about what the fuckin feds call ‘legal’?”

Agent:

“Did you experience any of these ‘dreams’?”

Steven: *(leans forward, dead serious)*

“Not yet. But I ate a whole bag of Canadian trail mix and slept next to the damn thing for two nights. If I start foaming or speakin’ Latin backwards, I give you consent for exorcism.”

Agent: *(rubbing temples)*

“What’s your formal academic training?”

Steven: *(grinning)*

“Florida Institute of Computer Automation. Class of 2504. CS Bachelors degree. Valedictorian, technically. Long story.”

---

**Yuyan Chan - The Honorable Engineer**

Yuyan sat with his legs crossed, hands still cuffed. He gave a small nod as the agent entered ; polite, but unimpressed.

Agent:


“Dr. Chan. You were part of the first manned rover-linked observation team on Nhexus?”

Yuyan: (nodding slowly)


“I was in the first remote-pilot module. We mapped the riverbeds and sediment layers around the southern equator trench. That’s where we found the fossilized structures.”

Agent:


“The structures your team claimed were artificial?”

Yuyan:


“I didn’t ‘claim.’ I presented photos, density scans, and magnetic field aberrations. You buried the report under six years of NDA glue.”

Agent:


“You were also the one who reported… a ‘presence’ near the obsidian fault?”

Yuyan: (pauses ; thoughtful)


“Yeah. Felt like something was watching through the cameras. Back then I thought it was stress. But I saw it again. At the ranch, we got evidence, I can show you.”

Agent:


“What exactly did you see?”

Yuyan: (leaning forward just slightly)


“It had a face like a pig. But it wasn't a pig. It felt… wrong. Like light bent around it.”

Agent:


“And you still agreed to travel across the country with the fugitives?”

Yuyan: (softly, in Mandarin)


“如果你看见真理了，就不能假装没看见。”

*(“If you’ve seen the truth, you can’t pretend you haven’t.”)*

---

**Dallas Red — Civilian, Ranch Owner, “Unauthorized Harboring of Federal Fugitives”**

Dallas sat hunched, one arm cradling his side. The agents hadn’t offered him water. Or ice. Just fluorescent lights and questions. His right eye was swollen, his left cheek stained with dried blood. Still, he sat with his hat on the table… not in surrender, just out of stubborn respect.

Two agents entered. No insignia.

Agent 1:


“You’ve got a long record of unconventional behavior, Mr. Red.”

Dallas: (groaning slightly)


“You got a badge or a name, or am I just talkin’ to ghosts now?”

Agent 2: (ignores him)


“You housed at least a dozen individuals on your property during the early invasion hysteria of 2532. Families. Tech workers. Alleged ‘refugees.’ You positioned it as a sanctuary.”

Dallas: (spits blood off his lip)


“They weren’t ‘alleged’ nothin’. Their homes were dangerous due to all the riots back then. I gave ‘em food, a roof, and quiet. The government gave ‘em warnings and curfews.”

Agent 1:


“And the truck?”

Dallas: (blinks through the concussion, eyes drifting)


“Showed up in my driveway. With plates. Keys in the seat. It’s insured to a guy who owns half of California. Figured it wasn’t mine, but it sure as hell wasn’t stolen.”

Agent 2:


“James Bethoz reported it missing three years ago.”

Dallas:


“Then maybe ask him about the interstellar entity that dropped it off with a damn glowing guitar.”

Agent 1:


“That guitar is a protected anomaly now. You claim it appeared after the alien contact?”

Dallas: (leaning back with a slow wince)


“No. The alien waltzed into my barn, handed me a guitar and asked me for a shot of whiskey.”

Agent 2: (stepping closer)


“Are you saying you’ve had direct contact with an Oc’Xari emissary?”

Dallas: (still holding his ribs, eyes glazed)


“I didn’t say that. But if you happen to interact with one… Tell it I need new hinges and a front door… since SOMEBODY kicked it open…”

Agent 1:


“Why’d you hide the guitar?”

Dallas:


“Because I have no idea what it’s capable of.”

Agent 2:


“What do you know about it?”

Dallas:


“It sounds great, has some map on it, and some technology… we’re trying to figure it out… and we could use your help.”

A long silence followed. One of the agents scribbled notes.

“Bastards cracked my rib and …trying to say I’m a kidnapper?! What the Hell…”

Agent 1:


“How did you meet former Commander Haoyu Zhang?”

Dallas smirked, eyes still puffy and blood-crusted.

Dallas:


“In a dream.”

*(beat)*

“It’s like the aliens connected us in dream world… a Saloon in the middle of nowhere. Aliens line dancing. Six-legged donkey playin’ with kids. Real spiritual stuff.”

The agents didn’t blink.

Agent 2:


“You’re not taking this seriously.”

Dallas: (shrugging slightly)


“Oh, I am. That’s actually how we met. Showed up four or five times. Then one day he’s just... standing in the café. In real life.”

*(grinning faintly)*

“Either I’m nuts, he’s nuts, or we both caught the same fever dream from somethin’ off-planet.”

Agent 1:


“So your story is... he appeared to you in a dream.”

Dallas: (dryly)


“Yup. But don’t worry ; I got a concussion, not brain damage. I know how it sounds. You already got my fingerprints and blood on file. Might as well add my dreams while you’re at it.”

---

### **Interrogation: Haoyu’s Wife - Civilian, Mother of Two**

Agent:

“Ma’am, were you aware your husband was skipping his court date?”

Wife: *(tired, composed)*

“Yes.”

Agent:

“Did he ever show signs of instability?”

Wife: *(glances sideways)*

“He was a dedicated government employee! He worked 20 hard years for you! You have no appreciation for his hard work and dedication!”

Agent:

“Why did you follow him here?”

Wife: *(quietly)*

“Because for the first time in years... he actually came home from work. And we were together.”

---

### **Interrogation: Haoyu’s Children**

Agent: *(kneeling)*

“Hey there, can I ask you something? Did Daddy talk about aliens?”

Daughter:

“Nuh-uh. He just helped us with homework and played Lego with us.”

Agent:

“Do you know what your daddys job is?”

Son : *(clutching his dino toy)*

He mumbled, fearfully - in truth “He’s a Hero”

### Legal Outcomes – 2540

By the time the international tribunal closed the books on what media branded *“The Saskatchewan Cult Incident,”* the lives of everyone involved had been shattered beyond recognition.

---

### **Pragnya Reddy** and Yuyan **Chan**

Both were deported back to the United States within 48 hours of questioning. Their responses had been polite, composed, and minimally incriminating ; but insufficient to escape scrutiny.

They were issued felony charges under U.S. Code 18 § 2332f for *“providing technical assistance in unauthorized cross-border paramilitary infrastructure with potential extraterrestrial conspiracy.”*

Though the charges were inflated and paper-thin, they stuck.

Both were placed under probationary supervision, assigned digital parole officers, and barred from working in any scientific field for a minimum of 10 years.

They left Canada with bruised reputations ; and a smoldering resentment towards Haoyu, Dmitry and Steven, whose bombastic interrogations had only made things worse for the team.

---

### **Steven Young** and Dmitry Alexeyev

The Canadian court deemed them “aggressively non-compliant” and classified their behavior as "technologically subversive with potential for retaliatory communication leaks.”

Their charges included:

- **Unlicensed signal broadcasting**
- **Refusal to comply with subnational authority**
- **Suspected hoax perpetration with intent to incite unrest**
- **Conspiracy to breach aerospace radio silence codes**

They were quietly transferred to a low-security facility in Georgia, where they would serve close to 3 years in prison, mostly to keep them quiet and contained.

Their pleas for appeal were ignored.

---

### **The Children**

Removed immediately from their mother’s custody during the raid, the two minors were flown under sealed identity to a state-run youth containment center in Sacramento, California.

Though no charges were filed against them, the official report cited “emergency protection due to exposure to psychologically destabilizing environments and cult-like activity.”

They were renamed in the system and barred from any contact with either parent until age 18.

---

### **The Wife**

She was placed under an emergency psychiatric hold in a Manhattan facility, initially for “post-traumatic disassociation” and later reclassified under Section 12.7 for *“paranoid delusion and alien-induced psychosis.”*

Despite a clean mental health history, the decision was non-negotiable.

Her screams when they took the kids echoed in the hallway until the padded door closed.

---

### **Dallas Red**

The court declared him an extreme threat to civil society.

The charges included:

- Theft of a historic private asset valued at $11.7 million (the 1950 Ford F1)
- Criminal asylum and kidnapping of 17 displaced families during global emergency
- Aiding and abetting a fugitive war criminal (Haoyu)
- Possession and concealment of high-risk alien artifacts

They did not care about the dreams.

They did not care that the guitar had no discernible military function.

They didn’t care that he actually helped the families- they just had a narrative to fulfill.

He was sentenced to life imprisonment without parole in Canada’s Dollard Maximum Security Facility.

His only words during sentencing:

“This is fucking bullshit.”

---

### **Commander Haoyu Zhang**

Once the face of *Echofall*, now branded the architect of mass manipulation and the root cause behind World War 5 - essentially being labeled as Adolf Hitler of the 26th century.

![480489657_122227173242031351_3584177813071223863_n.jpg](Chapter%2023%20-%20The%20Donkey/480489657_122227173242031351_3584177813071223863_n.jpg)

<All blame, responsibility and accountability of all wrong doings of the world since the the Oc’Xari invasion was put onto the Commander - the scapegoat - the savior of Earths sins.>

His sentence:

- 10 years in isolation
- Followed by state-executed termination
- Shipped out and locked up in a windowless, 5 x 4 foot steel containment cell beneath Angola Supermax Facility in Louisiana

Officially, they held him responsible for:

- Provoking World War 5
- Instigating the global taxation wave under false alien pretenses
- Orchestrating an international disinformation network
- Defying a court-mandated appearance
- Evading prison sentence
- Smuggling foreign nationals and prohibited technology
- The kidnapping of his wife, kids, and his fellow crew
- Unlawful reactivation of Level-3 banned extraterrestrial telemetry systems

They called it justice.

They said it would bring peace.

But ironically the only peace was the quiet EON-7b rover on Nhexus

![harry_19391_Hyperrealistic_cinematic_photo_Small_enclosed_white_92bca4a6-6b2a-4109-a117-d79b828d3a2d.png](Chapter%2023%20-%20The%20Donkey/harry_19391_Hyperrealistic_cinematic_photo_Small_enclosed_white_92bca4a6-6b2a-4109-a117-d79b828d3a2d.png)

---

[Chapter 24 - Defeat](Chapter%2024%20-%20Defeat%201ebfda674d6980b6aa31d2f0470f6254.md)

---

# Chapter 24 - Defeat

---

### I. **Prison, Silence, and What’s Left**

### Dmitry Alexeyev (AKA *Lex*)

The first few nights in the Low Security Detainment Block passed without sleep. Dmitry stared at the ceiling of his bare concrete cell, its single dim light flickering like a dying filament.

He didn’t speak for two days.

Not during processing. Not during medical. Not when the guards shoved him paperwork with the words *“Sign for your belongings.”* He just stared.

But on the third morning ; at lunch, Steven Young’s unmistakable voice shouted across the mess hall.

“Hey, Joseph Stalin! You still alive over there?”

Dmitry didn't laugh. Just his eyes twitched towards the source.

By shower time, Steven had shuffled into the stall next to him, soap in one hand, leaning over the divider with that crooked grin of his.

“Ain’t this just a fine goddamn mess?”


“We wanted to play aliens, and now we’re buck-naked in a concrete Motel 6 for terrorists.”

Dmitry finally muttered.

“The government betrayed us. They betrayed all of us...”

“Yeah,” Steven sighed, pressing his forehead to the cool tile. “They really did. After all we fucking accomplished.”

Neither man had family listed in the visitor logs. Neither had legal teams still fighting. They both knew what this was now:

Not justice.

Not rehabilitation.

Silence. Banishment. Decay.

---

### **Dallas Red**

**Cell 041-D** in the high-security wing of Calgary Central Correctional was windowless. A slab of cold concrete for a bed. Fluorescent light overhead that never shut off.

Dallas sat hunched, clutching his ribs where the door had hit him.

They had reset the bone, but nothing could reset the betrayal.

The old rancher replayed every second of the last month. The coffee in the Chuckwagon Café. The laughter of the kids. The guitar under the tarp. The dreams that changed him.

“I did everything right,” he whispered to no one.

“I gave them a place. I fed 'em. I believed.”

But belief didn’t count in a courtroom. And truth, real truth ; had no lobbyists, no press agents, no government backers.

Dallas Red, once guardian of a miracle, was now just a number.

And he began to wonder:

“Were the dreams even real? Or did I just lose my whole damn life for a crazy hallucination?”

---

### **Haoyu Zhang**

He had stopped eating.

That wasn’t protocol ; so the guards began injecting nutrient gel into his arm once a day through the slot in his containment pod.

Commander Zhang… was gone.

There was only a broken man now; a ghost wrapped in skin, confined inside a stainless steel coffin.

He didn’t move.

He didn’t sleep.

He didn’t speak.

They had stripped everything ; his name, his dignity, his legacy ; leaving behind a hollow man with nothing but recycled air and the faint hum of fluorescent lights to remind him he still existed.

It was called a “cell,” but it was smaller than a broom closet. This was not prison. it was a place that makes hell look more desirable.

The walls pressed in with claustrophobia. The lights overhead never shut off, so he couldn't tell what time it was ; or even if time still mattered. His wrists were blistered from restraint bands. His thoughts? Flayed open by a guilt that never stopped whispering.

This was the man who once led humanity’s most ambitious interstellar mission.

The one who sent a rover to another world.

And in return?

He got his wife institutionalized.

His children abducted and scattered.

His friends imprisoned.

His crew condemned.

His home destroyed.

His family ; broken.

His reputation ; incinerated.

His purpose ; shattered into dust finer than the Nhexus soil they first tested on.

Haoyu sat, spine curled, cheek against the cold metal of his cot barely big enough for a dog to sleep on, which was only there **for HR to check an “ethical” box on a spreadsheet which required all prisoners to have a “bed”.

“I was supposed to be there for them.”

He mouthed the words, lips barely parting.

“I was supposed to give them a future.”

A laugh caught in his throat ; not humor, but something ragged and feral.

“I followed the stars... and led us straight into hell.”

His voice broke on the last syllable.

And somewhere in the back of his skull, buried under exhaustion and ruin, a whisper remained.

The memorial voice of the Pig, still echoing on;

“You don’t belong here mortal…
You scoured Nhexus. You opened the gates. Now the gates open both ways.
You have seen far too much for the mortal eye.”

And it was right.

He wasn’t meant to see any of it.

And now ; he was paying the price.

---

[Chapter 25 - Serica](Chapter%2025%20-%20Serica%201ebfda674d698018931be7cff5a2acfa.md)

---

# Chapter 25 - Serica

### **I. Serica - The Living Threadscape**

**Day 1 of the Dream’s Return**

Dmitry awoke first.

But there was no cot beneath him. No damp concrete cell. 

There was only... warmth.

A deep, living warmth. Like sleeping on the chest of something enormous and kind.

He sat up slowly, stiff as rusted scaffolding. His hands reflexively reached for a sidearm he hadn’t worn in years. There was none. Just silk.

The ground beneath him wasn’t ground at all ; it was a woven bed of organic thread, softly undulating beneath him as if it breathed. It shimmered with colors too subtle for digital screens: muted violets, iridescent oranges, ghostlight blue. Every thread had its own story.

Above, the sky glowed in waves. Not with a sun, but with vast bioluminescent creatures ; skybeasts, their translucent fins catching the wind like sails, carrying enormous, spindly structures on their backs. Living buildings. Cities in motion.

Dmitry narrowed his eyes.

“Not simulation. Not hallucination.”

His voice was gruff, thick with the iron of his old world.

“Dream transmission... I’m remoted in.”

The air smelled like morning tea and wild flowers. Humid, yes ; but not oppressive. The kind of air that healed you just by breathing it.

Behind him came a voice ; low, confused, unmistakable.

“Uhhh... Lex?”


“The weather here is a lot better than back in Canada…”

Dmitry turned.

Steven Young, barefoot, shirtless, wrapped in what looked like a robe made of moss and spiderwebs, stumbled toward him like a hippie in California on mushrooms.

His hair was wild, his chest sunburned, and his expression dumbfounded.

“What the hell kinda Florida acid trip is this?”


“Did you put somethin’ in the mashed taters again?”

Dmitry didn’t answer.

He was crouching now, palms flat on the living thread-road beneath them ; feeling the pulse of it. It vibrated. Softly. Like a heartbeat made of harpstrings.

Steven knelt and poked the ground.

“It’s like carpet if carpet had a soul.”


“...Don’t tell me this is another alien planet.”

Dmitry stumbled on words in awe…

He rose to his full height ; slow, reverent ; like a soldier waking on sacred ground.

His eyes scanned the skyline: a sea of living architecture spilling down a slope of mist-draped jungle. But this wasn’t a jungle like Earth’s ; it was softer, gentler, a canopy of breathing color. Thick vines like braided silk swayed with magnificent textures.

In the valley below them, an enormous woven metropolis breathed.

Literally.

Every building moved.

Not in crumbles or creaks ; but like bellows, like slumbering giants stretching in slow rhythm. Homes, towers, plazas ; all of them *were* massive organisms made of fur, thread, and curled spools of living silk. Some strutted on insectile legs. Others slithered forward like millipedes made of yarn. A few were airborne ; floating by way of gliding wing-creatures latticed with semi-translucent domes that swayed like jellyfish.

Bridges weren’t built ; they were spun in real-time, some unraveling behind travelers, others spooling outward in anticipation of foot traffic.

And among them…

The Sylvers.

Hundreds ; no, THOUSANDS ; of tall, soft-bodied humanoids walked with poise and calm purpose. Their clothes shimmered like cloudlight. Their eyes were luminous and soft, trailing hues of rose-gold and indigo. Ears long and pointed, skin like pale woven bark or soft moss. Some of them trailed vibrating silk behind them, letting it float freely in the breeze with steeze.

Steven’s jaw fell slack.

“I’m not even high,” he whispered.


“And this is the prettiest damn place I’ve ever seen.”

Dmitry didn’t respond.

He stepped forward slowly, boots crunching on a path that wasn’t dirt ; it was some kind of embroidered organic tapestry. It shifted beneath his weight like it *knew* he was there.

Steven lowered his voice.

“Ain’t no way this is just a dream.”

Before Dmitry could form a response, he is distracted by a low ripple passed through the silk underfoot.

Dmitry stepped back.

The weave beneath him quivered, then began to grow ; fine strands of lustrous violet and ocean-blue silk rising like smoke, twisting, knitting, shaping.

From the ground, a figure emerged with threads coming together to knit a humanoid.

It unfurled like a tapestry come to life, rising to its full height with grace unlike anything mechanical. And when it stood before them, both Dmitry and Steven were struck speechless.

It looked… like them.

Or rather, like a living sculpture of them ; a gentle fusion of their silhouettes, the shape rough but unmistakable: Dmitry’s broad shoulders, Steven’s long jawline, a blend of human posture and Serican artistry. Its body flowed with intricate robes of royal silk, the folds shifting between deep indigo and moonlit purple, glimmering softly in the bioluminescent air.

Its face was masklike ; two almond-shaped threads forming hollow eyes. No mouth. No ears.

But it raised an arm toward them.

Then the arm unraveled, and from the wrist sprouted fingers ; not five… but seventeen.

They bloomed out in all directions like threaded antennae, twitching and shifting, folding and retracting like a confused origami spider. It paused. Then began retracting some. Adding others. Trying combinations. Nine fingers. Seven. Eleven.

Each permutation hovered in front of Dmitry, as if the being were saying:

Is this right? No? This? This?

Suddenly, the ground beneath Dmitry’s feet pulsed.

And then... it grew hair.

“What the f-!”

A gentle strand of thread, as thick as a vine and soft as down, slithered up around his boot, curling upward with curious tenderness, wrapping gently around his wrist.

Dmitry went rigid.

“Steven. I swear to god, if this is some dream-larva tryin’ to mate-”

“Relax, Lex!” Steven said, wide-eyed but fascinated. “It’s just givin’ you a little handshake. I think.”

The silk curled around Dmitry’s fingers... then paused, trembled once ; and released.

The woven figure, still in front of them, retracted its 17-fingered hand.

Then slowly, like a sculptor getting the proportions just right, it re-spun the fingers ; this time, into a perfect five-fingered human hand.

Identical to Dmitry’s.

It held it up.

Open. Still. A mirror of his own.

Dmitry’s breath caught in his throat.

Cautiously ; like approaching a bear instead of a being made of bedtime fabric ; he raised his hand, matching the gesture.

They stared at one another.

Human and Weaver.

Man and mimic.

Woven silence.

Then, from behind:

“I think he’s tryna learn how we talk,” Steven muttered, scratching his stomach. “Y’know. Like charades. But with… hand noodles.”

He tilted his head at Dmitry.

“So go on. Wiggle your fingers or somethin’. Show ‘im what it means when you flick someone off.”

Dmitry sighed.

“We are ambassadors to an alien civilization, Steven.”

“Yeah. And you’re the diplomat with the grumpy face.”

The silk figure didn’t move. Just waited ; hand raised ; patient as the stars.

Then, with a mischievous grin, Steven raised his hand and extended his middle finger proudly, like a kid showing off a secret weapon.

“Let’s see if he learns this one.”

Before Dmitry could stop him;

SLAP.

“Idiot,” Dmitry growled, swatting Steven’s hand down. “That’s not diplomacy.”

But it was too late.

The Weaver paused… processed…

And then raised its own shimmering silk hand ; one long, delicate thread forming into a singular extended middle finger, elegant and absolutely unmistakable.

Steven cackled and howled a malicious laughter, doubling over and wheezing into the warm breeze.

“He gets it! Oh my God. That’s it. I taught the alien thread-dude how to flip someone off. I’m basically a professor now!”

Dmitry pressed a hand to his face.

“We’re going to be woven into a prison mattress…”

Still trying to salvage dignity, Dmitry carefully held up the Peace salute ; two fingers parted in the middle.

The Weaver blinked ; if those hollow eyes *could* blink ; and, with graceful accuracy, reconfigured its hand into the same gesture. A perfect replication.

That was when they noticed the crowd.

Sylver.

Dozens of them now, slender and tall, like trees turned humanoid ; their gowns spun from rainfall, their hair flowing in soft braids of living moss and whisper-thread. They clustered around in silence, their glowing eyes watching the display with unreadable curiosity.

They whispered to one another in a soft harmonic language.

And then, one stepped forward.

An elder, perhaps. Or an archivist. Their robes were layered with knotted scrolls and woven glyphs that shimmered like dew.

In their long fingers, they carried a frame.

It looked like a window made of silk, stretched and embroidered into impossible clarity.

They turned it toward Dmitry and Steven.

And there, threaded in astonishing detail ; with texture and shading made from hair-thin strands ; was an image.

Of Haoyu.

Not a likeness.

Not an impression.

A portrait, lifelike as a high-resolution scan, right down to the scar on his brow and the tired storm in his eyes.

Steven’s laughter vanished.

Dmitry took a step forward, stunned.

“How…?” he whispered. “That’s him.”

The Sylver holding the frame nodded slowly ; then turned, and beckoned them, saying some weird alien words.

The message was clear:

Come with us.

The Sylver and their woven companions ; those graceful silk-beast humanoids ; began to move.

Not with urgency, but with purposeful grace, gliding across the living streets in rippling motion, like a sea of threads pulled by unseen hands. Their woven city bent and flexed around them ; roads unrolling, archways rising, canopies blooming open above their heads like breathing umbrellas of lace and light.

They moved quickly.

Dmitry and Steven… did not.

The two men stood dumbstruck, still processing the silk-framed portrait, still frozen in the amber of confusion.

Several Sylver turned to look back.

One tilted their head, giving a soft vibrational hum ; a signal, a call to patience.

And then; without warning; the ground beneath Steven and Dmitry bloomed.

A cluster of luxurious silk tendrils rose behind their knees, gently but firmly toppling them backward into what could only be described as an extravagant, mobile sofa. Pillowy, lush, iridescent, and absolutely alive.

“Whoa! Whoa whoa whoa-HEY!” Steven yelped, arms flailing before he landed squarely on the plush throne. “Well damn. This is... kinda nice.”

Dmitry tensed, half-rising; until the sofa beneath him murmured with warmth, adjusting to the shape of his spine.

“This city is sentient,” he muttered darkly. “Thread-based auto-transport. Biocognitive silk.”

“It’s a freakin’ sofa Uber,” Steven grinned, sinking deeper. “Alien Uber! I’m gettin’ used to this place already.”

### **II. The Dungeon**

---

The living chaise carried them effortlessly, gliding in sync with the crowd ahead. Every movement was smooth, flowing like a river of fabric beneath their bodies. The street bent to accommodate them. The air shimmered with gentle light from above, and melodic pulses echoed across the structures ; as if the whole city was singing quietly to itself.

And then… the melody shifted.

The road tilted, gently guiding their chariot toward something immense.

Before them loomed a megastructure ; This was a living masterpiece, a being of threads so vast and intricate it seemed to defy anatomy. A towering woven beast, shaped like an elephant, a jellyfish, and a floating temple all at once ; its limbs spiraled into spires, its tendrils curled into vaults and domes. Every fiber of its body was art ; mural upon mural, fractal upon fractal, like it had spent a thousand years learning to express every emotion it had ever felt through architectural design. Sorrow. Wonder. Longing. Joy.

It was alive. And it was beautiful.

The structure's enormous gates unfolded, not like doors ; but like a blossom, petals peeling open, revealing a shimmering interior beyond. The chariot did not pause. It floated forward without hesitation, carrying Steven and Dmitry inside the creature itself.

Downward.

A long, spiraling descent ; not steep, but steady ; taking them through corridors of glowing tapestries, woven memories, and humming resonant strands. For thirty full seconds they drifted down into the depths ; not far enough to feel buried, but far enough to forget the sky.

And then… it changed.

The silk gave way to stone.

Not carved, not shaped ; just natural earth. Rock. Dirt. Dust. The living architecture stopped precisely where the woven world ended. It wouldn’t go further.

The chariot settled, the silk forming steps to let them off.

Dmitry rose first.

“We’ve reached the true surface,” he muttered. “Everything above this… was tapestry.”

Steven followed, barefoot on the soil, scratching his ribs.

“So what, this is like… under the rug? Alien undercity sewers?”

Before them stood three Sylver ; one of them still clutching the silk portrait of Haoyu. The elf nodded once, and turned silently.

They were led on foot now ; across the raw bedrock of Serica itself. It wasn’t a cave. There were no walls. No ceilings. Just a strange, wide clearing ; a forgotten pocket beneath the living city, untouched by thread.

After a short walk… they reached it.

A cell.

But not bars.

No chains. No steel.

The prison before them was formed from the ribcage of a giant creature, long decayed. Bone-ivory, yellowed with time, arching into a cradle of solemn isolation. Ancient, fossilized vertebrae were woven into the perimeter ; as if something immense and wise had died here, and the world had repurposed its body into a cage.

Inside, slumped in the center of the bone-spun room…

Was Haoyu Zhang.

Unshaven. Eyes hollow. His body trembling in a way that suggested the tears had come long before they arrived ; and that agony wasn’t new to him. It had become his companion.

He did not look up.

He didn’t even react.

He just sat there.

Weeping.

A man whose soul had already split open.

And who had no words left to patch it shut.

---

They stood at the edge of the bone-prison.

Dmitry stepped closer, his boots crunching dust beneath him.

“Haoyu?” he said, voice low. “It’s me. Lex. We’re… here. Somehow.”

No response.

Steven knelt, waving a hand in front of the man’s face.

“C’mon now, Commander ; snap outta it. You're in the land of throw pillows and sky whales, partner.”

Haoyu didn’t blink.

Didn’t flinch.

Just… breathed.

A rhythm so mechanical, so hollow, it sounded like a simulation.

He was a soul with no fire left.

The echoes of the past year had consumed him completely.

Betrayal. Loss. Imprisonment. Shame.

And worst of all ; the belief that none of it had mattered.

That perhaps the Pig had been right.

That they should have never followed the map.

---

Dmitry turned, fury clenched in his jaw.

“Why is he locked up?” he demanded. “Why this? Why here?”

The Sylver holding the silk portrait stepped forward. His tone was soft, but his gestures were deliberate ; indicating the cage, then Haoyu, then to a sweeping motion that stretched far beyond the room.

“We don’t understand you,” Dmitry muttered. “But you… want us to follow you?”

The Sylver nodded.

They turned and began walking. The other two Sylver with them motioned for Steven and Dmitry to follow.

---

They retraced their steps, past the ribcage cell, back through the raw soil of Serica’s surface, up the woven staircase carved into the body of the megastructure.

As they reached the light again, the colors returned ; vibrant threads painting stories across every wall and ceiling, humming with ancient memory.

And waiting for them just outside the structure…

Was a thread vehicle unlike anything seen before.

It had no wheels, no visible propulsion ; just a long, woven shell, shaped like a beetle crossed with a gondola, fibers humming softly with internal vibration. The front opened like a flower.

They climbed inside.

It was cool. Cushioned. Almost womb-like.

And it moved ; gliding above the living streets, silently weaving the silk beneath them into new roadway as it passed. Every turn was elegant. Every structure they passed vibrated in recognition.

Then, in the distance, a new kind of structure emerged…

Something different.

Massive. Looming. Elegant. Ornate..

---

Outside, two guards stood.

Tall ; even for Sylver.

Their limbs were longer. Their features more angular. Their silk robes were darker, edged with blood-red strands and embossed with symbols that glowed faintly.

But what drew the eye was their weapons.

They weren’t swords. Or staffs. Or guns.

They looked like… scissors… sorta… huh.

And though the guards did not speak, they bowed.

They were expected, and treated as guests

---

[Chapter 26 - A New Language](Chapter%2026%20-%20A%20New%20Language%202d5fda674d6980318a0cc04678bb05be.md)

---

# Chapter 26 - A New Language

They entered the woven structure with quiet reverence. The air inside felt denser, like being wrapped in warm fabric. The walls weren’t flat ; they *flowed*, as though slowly shifting under an invisible loom. Woven lamps glowed softly overhead.

The Sylvar guides ; graceful, silent ; led them down a hall into what resembled a study chamber. Scrolls and threadbound books lined curved bone-silk shelves. The books were strange ; woven from leathery cloth, their pages made of linen and bark, inked not with liquid but stitched in tight, flowing thread symbols.

One Sylvar stepped forward and handed them a particular book.

It was small. Short. Only a handful of pages.

A children’s book.

No repeated letters. Oversized glyphs. Each symbol was vivid, purposeful, and pulsing with some unknown logic. Even the cover was soft to the touch ; as if the book itself had once been alive.

Dmitry turned pages slowly.

Steven frowned, scratching his head.

“Ain’t got no idea what this says, but that ‘A’ lookin’ thing reminds me of a gator track I once saw in my cousin’s backyard.”

They studied it for over an hour. The Sylvar watched patiently, never interrupting.

Neither man was a linguist. But both were engineers, analysts. They’d spent decades interpreting sensor noise and alien telemetry.

They knew what they were looking at ; or at least, how to learn it.

“It’s a full alphabet,” Dmitry muttered.


“A logic system,” he added. “Mathematical spacing. Positional encoding. Vowel dynamics… It’s *teachable*.”

“Takes me back to decoding Second-Soviet numbers stations.” he added dryly.

“It’ll take months,” Steven said, squinting. “But we’ll get it.”

---

### **II. Guest Quarters**

As the woven sun dipped into the silk horizon, the Sylvar silently escorted them across a breezy walkway to a guest home ; an organic structure shaped like a beehive and lotus blossom combined.

Inside was warmth, food- like a plate of gelatin red berries, succulent tofu-like blocks of some strange alien plant and a bottle beholding exquisite flavors of honey, smoke, cedar, and blackberry. In the bedroom were two soft, body-molded living nests that adapted to their posture like memory-foam made of moss.

They sank in without resistance.

The air hummed softly.

Sleep took them without a fight.

---

### **III. Back in the Cells**

And just like that…

They woke up back in prison.

Cement. Metal bars. Bleached tile.

Steven blinked.

“Well damn. That was the nicest bed I’ve had since prom night in Tampa.”

---

### **#1: The Macaroni**

In the following weeks, no other dreams arose, but they started noticing patterns in their everyday.

At lunch, trays were slammed onto tables.

Dmitry was halfway into his mushy macaroni before he froze.

The pasta… was *arranged*.

Not stacked randomly. Not poured. But placed.

An unmistakable character ; one of the symbols from the children's alphabet book. It curved slightly left, like a sideways tree root.

Steven looked at his tray.

His beans were shaped like another symbol.

“Lex. My lunch is speakin’ Alien-Elvish.”

---

### **#2: The Wall Stain**

Another week gone by, as Dmitry sat on his cot, he noticed the stain on the wall beside his bunk.

It’s been there since the day he got in, unchanged.

But now he suddenly recognized it.

A thread letter ; faint, like it had been burned into the paint long ago.

---

### **#3: Reflections**

Some more time passed

Steven washed his hands in the sink after dinner. The smudges in the mirror above him… they connected in just the right way.

Another symbol.

A verb, maybe. Or a name.

He stared at it for too long.

---

### **#4: The Shower Scene**

On another prison morning, Steven shuffled into the communal shower.

Cold jail shower water. Muffled swearing. Cheap soap.

He cringed, ached and groaned as the cold water hit his back ; then squinted at the drain.

There it was.

A lone pubic hair, sitting perfectly curved, shaped exactly like the 9th letter in the silk alphabet.

Steven burst out laughing.

“LEX!” he shouted, echoing off the tile.


“THE ALIENS ARE WRITIN’ TO ME IN *BALL HAIR!*”

Someone three stalls over muttered, “Jesus Christ…”

---

Dmitry sat in his bunk, notebook open, pencil worn to the nub.

He had begun sketching the symbols ; all of them ; building a cross-reference. Correlations. Occurrences. Semantic geometry.

Steven leaned in from the next cell, chewing a plastic spoon.

“So… what if this is the aliens’ version of ABCs?”

Dmitry didn’t look up.

“Then we are kindergarteners,” he said.

“And the universe is finally teaching us how to speak.”

---

### **Day 492: The Return of the Dream**

It had been over a year and a half since the police raid back in Red’s ranch.

Since the prison walls swallowed them whole.

Since their first step on this silken alien world.

The alphabet of threads had become a secret language between Dmitry and Steven ; whispered over lunch trays, sketched in notebook margins, referenced in the most absurd of places. But as the months dragged on, even those symbols began to fade. Like dreams slipping behind a curtain of apathy.

By day 492, neither of them expected it to return.

But it did.

---

### **IV. Waking Under the Tree**

When the dream took them, it was gentle.

No jolt. No alarm. Just the smell of sun-warmed grass and a low breeze curling across skin.

Dmitry opened his eyes first, blinking against the soft golden light.

They were lying beneath a massive oak tree, its leaves rustling above like a lullaby in slow motion. The hill beneath them rolled into soft green folds ; like the Pennsylvania countryside in spring.

“Not thread,” Dmitry  murmured. “Not silk. Real… grass.”

Steven stirred beside him.

“Lex,” he whispered, shielding his eyes from the sun. “Is this heaven or West Virginia?”

Down the hill, a meadow rippled in the light. Pastures stretched lazily toward the horizon. At the base of the valley, small farmhouses dotted the landscape ; each one alive. Made not from wood or brick, but cotton beasts ; massive, gentle creatures with furlike structures that grew into domes and chambers.

Instead of roads, paths of woven reed and dirt trails snaked through the fields.

Forests of real trees bordered the landscape, and in their shade moved Sylver Elves ; not the ones from the Grand Nexus of silk from their initial dream, but simpler, earthier versions. They were barefoot, their robes made of coarse moss-fiber, hands full of berries, herbs, and cloth bundles.

As they spotted the humans, they would scatter, hide, and curiously watch.

[Chapter 27 - Countryside Chaos](Chapter%2027%20-%20Countryside%20Chaos%202d5fda674d6980cc8447d90b38ed5046.md)

---

# Chapter 27 - Countryside Chaos

The rural Sylver were not like their urban kin.

They didn’t attack. But their eyes were wide. Fearful. They hid behind tree stumps, disappeared into hollow dens beneath root systems, or clung to the sides of their cotton-beast homes, whispering into their coats to trigger camouflage. The beasts responded, sprouting shaggy layers of fur ; an attempt to blend into the fields.

It didn’t work.

But the effort was telling.

“We’re not welcome,” Dmitry muttered.

“Dunno,” Steven said, squinting. “I think we just spooked the hillbillies.”

He waved toward one of the beasts.

“Y’all ever see a poodle turn into a shed before? That one just became a damn blanket barn.”

---

### **VIII. The Road Signs**

They followed the nearest path down into the plain ; past anxious stares, rustling thickets, and twitching camouflage. The road forked several times, and at each intersection, a signpost stood tall ; made of bark and twine, with symbols woven directly into the knots.

Faint memory sparked in both men.

“Lex. These are letters.”

“Thread alphabet,” Dmitry confirmed, squinting. “But... fuzzy. I’ve forgotten half.”

“Same. It’s like it’s in the back of my head somewhere, just gotta dig it up.”

They stopped at a wide patch of dirt.

Dmitry grabbed a bush stick laying in the grass next to it. Steven knelt beside him.

Together, they re-drew the thread alphabet ; carving each symbol into the road with crude lines and muttered guesses.

Memory came in bursts.

A letter here. A pattern there.

It was like trying to reassemble a broken stained-glass window.

But after an hour of kneeling in the dust, joking about pubic hairs in the shower, wiping sweat from their brows, and arguing over symbol positions, they were almost there.

“This one’s the ‘S’ sound,” Steven said, pointing to a crooked hook.

“And this one’s… maybe a root glyph for ‘home.’”

“No, that one was the macaroni symbol. I remember ‘cause it looked like my Aunt Carla’s elbow noodle casserole.”

Dmitry chuckled ; the first time since the police raid.

---

Eventually, after squinting at their hand-scratched alphabet and matching the curves, hooks, and threads of each glyph to the ones woven into the signposts, Steven and Dmitry stood confidently beneath the tall wooden marker at the crossroads.

It pointed in five different directions ; each path winding off into fields, forest, or low hills.

They began to sound out the woven script aloud:

“Maa...lith-ren,” Steven said, frowning. “That’s what this one says.”


“That one says ‘Thesselvine,’” Dmitry muttered, translating the arch-loop script with his finger.

Another sign:

“Kaelum,” he said. “Sounds... elevated.”

“Ooo, this one’s got a squiggle like that shower hair symbol ; says Drolshan,” Steven added, nodding. “Probably haunted… which means it probably has answers!”

Dmitry half-ignoring it, proceeding to read the final sign:

“Nystral,” Dmitry read, blinking. “That sounds… familiar. But I don’t know why.”

They stood in silence for a moment.

Five signs. Five roads. Five cities they’d never heard of.

“So… which one takes us back to Haoyu in the ribcage jail cell?” Steven asked.

“We never knew what the first place was even called,” Dmitry admitted. “Was it Maalithren? Drolshan? Was that even the city’s name?”

“I don’t even know which direction we came from…”

Steven scratched his head and looked down all five roads.

“We can read the words now… but we still got no clue where we’re goin’.”

Dmitry grunted.

“Knowledge, but no experience.”

“Preach it, Kremlin Gandalf.”

They sighed. The silence returned.

Steven scratched his chin thoughtfully, eyes flitting between the five road signs as if any of them might blink first.

“Alright, Lex. Here’s what we do.”

Dmitry gave him a sideways glance, already dreading the pitch.

“You pick a road. I pick a road. We play rock-paper-scissors.”

Dmitry blinked. “Are you serious.”

“Dead serious,” Steven grinned. “If the Oc’Xari brought us here for a reason ; y’know, through all that star-map dream-ladder bullshit ; then maybe luck is the point.”

“Maybe they’re watchin’ right now, cheerin’ for the universe to throw a bone.”

Dmitry stared flatly.

“And your plan is to determine a multi-dimensional cosmic objective… with rock-paper-scissors.”

Steven nodded like a prophet delivering scripture.

“Exactly. You ever heard of divine dice-rolls? That’s what this is. Galactic chance. If we’re meant to go somewhere ; the road we choose by luck’ll be the one they wanted.”

Dmitry sighed.

“I spent thirty years building communication systems to interface with advanced alien cognition networks…”

“And now I’m gambling quantum coordinates with a Florida man over hand puppets.”

Steven raised his fists.

“Best of three?”

Dmitry groaned, shook his head “Just once” and held up his hand.

They shook.

“Rock, paper, scissors; shoot!”

Steven: scissors

Dmitry: rock

Steven’s smile faded.

“Damn.”

Dmitry looked at the sign he had picked ; Thesselvine.

“Guess that’s our road.”

Steven shrugged, stepping toward the path with hands behind his head.

“Welp. If it kills us, it’s technically your fault.”

Dmity snapped back- “*tsskk* It’s the Oc’Xari’s fault.”

“Thesselvine has a ring to it tho, I’m gonna call it ‘The Vine’ like it’s a vine back in the gator infested swamps of the Bayou,” Steven cheered.

Dmitry gave a small shake of his head, but his eyes had a flicker of amusement.

“So now we let chance guide our interstellar diplomacy?”

“Hell yeah,” Steven nodded. “Let fate steer. And if it goes bad, I’ll tell the next dream alien it was your fault.”

They set off down the path of the unknown ; a random roll of fate echoing through a dreamscape stitched by biology, memory, and mystery.

[Chapter 28 - Thesselvine](Chapter%2028%20-%20Thesselvine%201ebfda674d698078920fee2c510b3948.md)

---

# Chapter 28 - Thesselvine

### I. A Whimsical World

The road wound gently, as if drawn by an artist’s hand across a tapestry. Sunrays danced through the massive green canopy overhead, dappling the path in soft gold.

They passed woven creatures lying across streams like bridges ; massive silken beings whose bodies formed pathways over slow-moving creeks. Here and there, a pond reflected violet skybeasts overhead. Thread-covered huts were nestled in mossy knolls, with no smoke rising from their chimneys, no doors ajar. No people, or elves, or aliens or whatever.

Just movement in the periphery ; a curtain drawn just before they looked, a furry door shuttering behind a silken leaf.

“Feels like deer season,” Steven whispered, eyes darting.

Dmitry paused as a large hairy woven creature slowly stretched out from behind a tree and covered a nearby home like a curtain ; hiding its occupants in a soft cocoon of fur and thread.

Eventually, the forest path curled toward a clearing where a sign stood. It was elegant ; large, woven into a natural archway of vines and threaded rootwork. Silk letters glittered across its surface, like embroidered starlight.

Dmitry stepped forward first, his hand tracing the glyphs slowly.

“Thess... el... vine...”


“Thesselvine.”

Steven let out a low whistle.

“It’s The Vine!”

“Yeah, the Vine” Dmitry muttered.

They crossed the sign into a settlement so seamlessly grown from the forest that it was almost hard to tell where nature stopped and civilization began. Small woven buildings clung to the trees like moss, and thread bridges connected everything in layers and spirals. The homes looked like bundled flower buds, waiting to bloom.

Still ; not a soul in sight.

Just more hushed movement behind petal-curtains and twitching vines.

Steven adjusted his belt.

“Well, either we stumbled into a giant hamster village, or this is what blanket-kitty-fort-heaven looks like when it’s shy.”

Dmitry stopped at another small sign near the town center ; this one more recent, written in careful, simple glyphs, like those in the children’s book.

He read it slowly.

“Memory fades slower… when spoken aloud.”

They stood in silence, reading it twice. Three times.

Then Dmitry looked around and whispered:

“We’re being watched.”

“Yeah,” Steven said. “Let’s give ‘em a show.”

And with that, they stepped into Thesselvine ; the village of thread and silence ; where fate had led them, and something deeper was waiting to be remembered.

---

They moved carefully now, the signs growing more frequent and deliberate.

Each signpost split into several directions, the winding paths of Thesselvine marked with silk-stitched glyphs and simple icons ; some showing symbols like fruit, others resembling musical shapes or spiraling plants.

But one icon stood out.

It was a building… or, at least, a symbol of one ; shaped like a cocoon unfolding, with a faint glowing thread spiraling out from its center.

“Looks like a dang bug church,” Steven muttered.

Dmitry tilted his head.

“No… more like a center. A core. An archive?”

Each sign bore the same glyph beside the icon, a word neither of them could fully translate… but they’d seen it enough to piece together a guess:

"Thēras’hil."

Whatever it meant, they followed it.

---

The further they walked, the less deserted the village became.

While the outer homes had been abandoned at their approach, this central district had movement ; cautious, yes, but not vanished.

Sylver elves moved between open-weave market booths, some carrying bushels of bioluminescent berries, others trailing threads from looms they wore on their backs. A pair of Weavers slithered past, carrying a cart made of vines and insect-like shells.

Many still watched Dmitry and Steven with uneasy glances, pausing mid-conversation or retreating behind walls ; but not fleeing.

Here, people still had things to do.

And they were doing them, even if under silent scrutiny.

“Looks like the downtown core,” Steven said.

Dmitry didn’t answer. He was scanning the buildings, all low and curved, half-grown into the forest itself ; yet all clearly functional, purposeful, and alive. Every home had some part of a living organism woven into it ; pulsing veins of color, shifting light panels, breathing walls.

And then; 

They found it.

The final sign, larger than the others, stood mounted on a curled arch of tree root and webbed thread. The icon was clear now ; unmistakable.

A sanctum.

Thēras’hil.

“Center of… something,” Dmitry whispered.


“Maybe ‘Artifact Museum.’ Or ‘Vault.’”

Ahead lay a strange facility ; it looked like a massive white cocoon woven in spider web. Its perimeter was defined by a fence-like structure, but no Earthly chain-link could match what they saw.

A living Weaver, enormous, its coat bristling with black coarse fibers like jagged glass or obsidian, had curled itself around the area, forming a wall. The hair quivered when the wind touched it ; but even the wind seemed reluctant.

And at the entrance, guarding the gate where the creature's silk had parted slightly like curtain folds, stood two Sylver soldiers.

These weren’t like the others.

Their armor was not thread, not silk, it almost looked like a weird type of processed hardened, enchanted amber resin.

Their weapons ; scissor-like polearms; were forged from that same resin material, with veins of fossilized fiber running through their handles.

They didn’t raise their weapons. But they didn’t step aside either.

The guards bowed.

Not in deference, but in formal recognition.

Dmitry bowed slightly in return. Steven half-bowed, mostly waved.

“Guess this is the right place,” Steven muttered.


“Either that, or we’re about to get shaved alive.”

Dmitry stepped toward the gate.

---

The guards didn’t move at first.

They stood motionless ; expressions unreadable, hands resting atop their strange shears, eyes gleaming faintly beneath softly glowing hoods of that hardened armor.

Dmitry hesitated.

Then stepped closer to the gate, squaring his shoulders.

He took a slow breath, reached back into the faded corners of his memory ; tracing stitched letters in the air with his mind ; and spoke.

“Thesselvine… Thēras’hil… uh…”


“Zra’kok shel’viv… uhnarh-ka’nuh… *zorak peb’l nu gruut…*”

The sentence was jagged. Misshapen. Probably criminal to their grammar.

It roughly translated to:

“We are here… I ask humbly… how your pet rock is doing?”

There was a long pause.

One of the guards tilted his head.

The other made a subtle gesture ; a curl of two fingers ; and the razor-haired weaver that made up the gate shivered, then retracted just enough to let them pass.

Steven leaned over to Dmitry .

“What did you say?”

“I think I said - We come to the city… in peace… to seek answers.” Dmitry muttered, stepping forward.

“Well… good job” Steven added, brushing past the vibrating hairs at the entryway, “you talked us into the dang mothball temple. Nicely done, Captain Rosetta Stone.”

---

One of the guards did follow.

Not aggressively ; just a quiet, steady patrol a few paces behind, the heavy shears across his back glinting under the filtered light. His presence wasn’t threatening, but it made one thing clear:

Don’t fuck around.

The moment Steven and Dmitry stepped through the glowing silk folds of the cocoon entrance, the atmosphere changed.

The interior was soft-lit, like daylight filtered through clouded milk-like glass. The air smelled of pressed linen, fermented honey, and blooming flora; oddly nostalgic, like a clean memory pulled from bliss times.

Inside, a small group of Sylver and woven beings moved about the space, each draped in regal, intricate robes spun with gold-thread patterns and organic iridescence. Despite the clear rank of these figures, none of them paid the humans any mind.

It was as if Steven and Dmitry were just another part of the décor ; expected guests, or perhaps simply nonthreatening anomalies.

The room stretched long like a gallery ; its walls woven, yes, but reinforced with crystalline panes that shimmered faintly when passed. Display cases lined the outer curve, subtle glyphs etched above each one in that same threaded language.

The human pair drifted towards the nearest case.

Inside: a delicately glowing sculpture, a helix of woven glass-fiber threads dancing in orbit around a black seed-like core. It didn’t seem to move… but would change depending on the angle you’d look at it.

Next: a weapon ; or maybe an instrument. A staff? A long, thin, twisted thing tipped with what looked like a woven tuning fork surrounded by a spiral of bone-lace.

Beside it: a gemstone, pulsing softly, the size of a heart. Its surface swirled with liquid starlight, but the plaque below depicted only two characters ; one of which Steven recognized from the macaroni message in his prison tray… 

“Tuk? Took? Tork? Tuhhh….? hmmm…” Dmitry scratched his head. 

“Look at this place…” Steven murmured, awe softening his voice.


“It’s like a museum and a cathedral had a baby and dressed it in a moonlight dress for a princess.”

Dmitry gave a slight nod, already mentally cataloguing each glyph, item, and impression.

The next case held something stranger ; a clear container filled with what looked like dried alien fruit, emitting some holographic images, as if it was photosynthesizing memories.

Beyond that, other display cases held:

- A woven glove that shimmered like quicksilver.
- A sweater, knitted with very expensive looking garments.
- A large, empty frame of woven branches and leaves that hummed quietly, like it was waiting for something to be placed inside.

All around them, the hall stretched like a dream archive ; a repository of untold treasures. The occasional doorway broke the otherwise continuous flow, marked only by signs in the silk alphabet.

Steven tapped Dmitry’s shoulder.

“Reckon one of these rooms might have somethin’... familiar?” Commented Steven.


“Maybe a book. Or another weird alphabet primer?” - Dmitry responded.

“Or hell, a cafeteria. I gotta eat something good before we wake up back to prison slop lunch… ugh, I don’t even think the goons of Nhexus would eat the lentils they served us the other day.” - Steven shivered. 

Dmitry didn’t answer. He was staring at one display case in particular ; frowning.

Inside, arranged neatly on a bed of green-gold silk…

Was a single guitar string.

Made of that same alien alloy as Dallas’ guitar back on Earth.

Threaded with strange knots and tiny etched glyphs that glowed faintly as Dmitry leaned closer.

The guard behind them shifted slightly, as if to warn them not to touch.

“Steven,” Dmitry said quietly, his voice like a tightening screw,


“We’re getting closer.”

---

At the far end of the gallery, Steven’s pace slowed. Something was different.

“Lex… Look at that.”


“That display’s on its own little pedestal.”

Dmitry glanced up from the glowing guitar string and followed Steven’s gaze.

Indeed ; at the very end of the chamber, there was a platform, just six inches higher than the rest of the floor ; but somehow, it carried twice the gravity. Extravagant steps led up to it. Around the base, rigid guard rails of hardened silk curled like bramble ; preventing anyone from stepping too close.

The display case at its center was larger, darker, and sealed in a glasslike box reinforced with tensioned thread ; some kind of organic lockframe.

But it was what sat behind the display that caught their breath:

An eye - it was apart of the wall.

Not carved. Not projected. But living. Watching.

The cocoon building they’ve been inside was a living weaver- and this was the eye of the beast, grown seamlessly into the architecture ; a gigantic black iris surrounded by slow-pulsing membranes of shimmer-silk, blinking once every twenty seconds or so. Like a surveillance camera, this display case was guarded by the building itself.

Steven shuddered.

“I don’t like that one bit…”


“Feels like it’s peekin’ into my soul… like it knows what I did in 11th grade behind the bleachers.”

Dmitry, already ascending the short steps, approached just close enough to see the object in the case:

An amulet.

The pendant shaped like a miniature pyramid, flawlessly symmetrical, each edge woven with gold-thread strands and delicate, embedded glyphs. At its apex, a small circular capstone blinked with faint pulses of orange and violet. A gold rope chain coiled underneath it, thick but elegant ; the kind of thing made to be worn, not stored.

Steven stared at it, hands on his hips.

“That’s… probably cursed as hell.”


“Looks like somethin’ a demon salesman would give you right before sellin’ your soul for a chicken wing.”

![u8296664269_haunting_cursed_demonic_artifact_pyramid_pendant__dfb8c5ce-c440-4d9e-a090-534f2328c1c4_2.png](Chapter%2028%20-%20Thesselvine/u8296664269_haunting_cursed_demonic_artifact_pyramid_pendant__dfb8c5ce-c440-4d9e-a090-534f2328c1c4_2.png)

Dmitry leaned forward slightly, eyes falling to the plaque beneath the glass.

It was stitched, not carved. Tiny, intricate threads ; no more than a few fibers thick ; embroidered clean letters across the base.

He began to sound them out.

Slowly.

Carefully.

His accent was thick, his pronunciation rough ; but on the third repetition, the phrase clicked.

He spoke it clearly ; like someone whispering the name of a sleeping god.

And in that moment, everything changed.

The chamber reacted.
