Dmitry’s stomach plummeted as the officer approached.

“Hey ; just a heads-up,” the officer said casually.


“There was an avalanche just east of here, and there’s a heavy snowstorm warning between us and Calgary. The roads are closed. If I were you? I’d hunker down here for the night.”

Without waiting for a response, the officer turned and strolled into the gas station mini-mart.

Dmitry let out a long, tension-fueled breath.

“Whew… that was a close one.”

Steven ungripped his glock, relaxed, and leaned back in the passenger seat, looking at the snow-clouds rolling in overhead.

“Guess we’re staying in Gas Station Toilet Buttfuck Mountain Town tonight,” he said with that same deadpan Florida charm.

A short drive later, they found the nearest motel.

It looked newer than the last one, but the price was almost double. Still rundown, still half-buried in snow, but at least the neon vacancy sign was on.

Dmitry planned; “Let’s go in, if we can get a room, lets come back out and move the car.”

Inside the lobby, the air smelled pleasant of pine and Christmas scents. The staff behind the counter seemed immediately annoyed when Dmitry tried to pay with American cash.

“We don’t accept cash,” the clerk said with suspicion, glancing at their unshaven faces, ratty coats, and generally apocalyptic look.

But the pleading from Dmitry, and Steven’s annoyed:

“You want us to die in a snowstorm?”

…somehow swayed the man’s logic.

With great reluctance, the clerk counted the stack of dollar bills and slid them a keycard.

---

As soon as the motel key was in their hands, Dmitry told Steven “I’m going to move the car.” as he bolted out the door, leaving Steven behind in the lobby.

He ran out to where his stolen beater was parked, engine still warm under the snowfall. First thing he did was wipe down the steering wheel, gearshift, door handles, dash; everything; with a bleach-soaked rag he pulled from a ziplock bag.

The scent was harsh. Acrid. Chemical paranoia in cloth form.

He peeled out the glove compartment contents, tore out any receipts, wrappers, gum, anything that might even *hint* at who they were. Tossed it all into a grocery bag, stuffed it in a public trash bin down the street. Then he backed the car out, turned down a residential back road, and parked it five blocks away beneath a snow-heavy cedar tree.

Dmitry wiped the door handles again for good measure, shut it softly, and pulled up his hoodie.

He was about halfway back when he looked down.

Footprints.

His boots were punching clear, deep marks into the fresh powder.

He froze - Paranoia overwhelming…

Then sighed.

“Snowstorm’s coming anyway,” he muttered to himself.


“They’ll be buried within an hour.”

He kept jogging, breath puffing white in the mountain air. By the time he made it back to the motel, snow had already started drifting sideways. The storm was arriving right on cue.

Inside, a warm, log cabin, ski resort type room, with a rocking chair, wooden beds, and a few animal taxidermy heads hung on the walls. Steven was already relaxed, lying sideways on the double bed, TV flickering blue light across his face as some ancient sitcom played.

“They got a deer head, bear head, fox head… no pig head.” Steven observed.

“The pig should come and protest. Put up a pig head or die in eternal hellfire.” Dmitry joked as he kicked off his boots, locked the door, and got to work.

He dragged the wooden chair from the corner across the carpet and jammed it under the doorknob, just like before. Then made his rounds ; opening drawers, sliding back the curtains an inch, checking vents, peeking into the motel closet, opening the bathroom, peeking behind the shower curtain. No shadows. No whispers. 

He let out a slow, heavy sigh and finally settled near the end of the bed, still tense.

“You think Piggie’s gonna be in the bathroom this time,” he asked, “or hiding in the closet to give his nightly sermon?”

Steven smirked without looking up from the TV.

“I dunno, man. I hope he’s out there preaching to the snowstorm. Maybe it’ll make a deal with it to fuck off.”

Dmitry chuckled and leaned his head back against the wall.

The wind outside began to howl like wolves.

But for now, at least, the room was quiet.

---

Five days.

That’s what they thought, murmured, and etched silently in their minds before the motel room dimmed into sleep.

The night wasn’t quiet, but it was strangely peaceful. The blizzard howled like a pack of arctic beasts outside their thin motel walls, winds screaming, snow pelting sideways like a million shattered needles. But the room was warm, smelled like pine, the mattress soft.

They slept like babies.

Dreamless, merciful sleep.

---

8:30 AM

A mechanical buzzing from the nightstand clock. Annoying and shrill.

Steven groaned.

Dmitry sat up slowly, swung his legs off the side of the bed, and blinked the blur from his vision.

He walked to the window and drew the curtain back just a crack.

“Well, shit,” he muttered.

A solid sheet of white covered the town. Cars, sidewalks, lamp posts; everything had been buried beneath what looked like ten feet of fresh powder. And it was still falling. The wind still shrieking.

Behind him, Steven was rubbing his face.

“How’s it look, Captain?” he asked, voice still lazy with sleep.

Dmitry didn’t turn away from the glass.

“There’s not a single car moving through the snow. Not one. Roads are dead.”

Steven reached lazily for the TV remote, flicked it on; static.

He flipped through the channels. Still static.

“Guess the storm took out cable.”

He pulled out his phone. “No bars.”

They both sighed in sync.

They chewed through dry granola bars, cracked open a couple bottles of water, and took turns showering for real this time; long, hot, quiet showers, washing away the stale motel stink of yesterday’s survival. The storm boomed like war drums outside, but inside, they were trying to pretend; just for a moment; that this was normal.

By 10:55, they packed up their gear and went down to check out.

---

The lobby was crowded.

Couples in parkas. Families. Older folks still in pajamas. Travelers with sleds. A woman clutching a suitcase and her teacup poodle. All gathered around a uniformed man in a blue parka; his badge visible.

It was the same officer from the gas station the day before.

His voice was calm, professional, trying to carry authority and friendliness all at once.

“Last night,” he said, “an avalanche took out a few of our local cell towers. Luckily, nobody was hurt. But I do need to give you an update about the weather.”

Dmitry and Steven exchanged a glance.

“This storm…” the officer continued, “is not your average snow dump. They’re calling it a superstorm. One of the worst to ever hit the interior. It’s expected to rage for the next four to five days. That’s the forecast, and believe me; if it clears up sooner, we’ll let you know.”

There were groans.

Some gasps.

One guy at the back dropped his suitcase and muttered, “Jesus Christ.”

The officer raised a hand.

“I know it’s not what you want to hear. But we do have some good news. The province of British Columbia has declared this an emergency weather lockdown, and the government will fully compensate your motel stay until the storm ends.”

Half the room cheered. The other half muttered curses.

“So,” he smiled, trying to lighten the mood, “think of this as an unexpected free vacation. Revelstoke’s a beautiful place this time of year. We’ve got some great little craft breweries, world-class snowboarding slopes, a couple steakhouses, a hotspring thermal bathhouse, cozy cabins, and a museum for anyone who likes a bit of local history. Try to make the most of it, folks.”

He smiled again and turned to speak with the desk staff.

![u8296664269_police_officer_in_hotel_lobby_speaking_with_crowd_a8e28498-3c70-4687-906e-9deb37ab1ce2_3.png](Chapter%2036%20-%20British%20Columbia/u8296664269_police_officer_in_hotel_lobby_speaking_with_crowd_a8e28498-3c70-4687-906e-9deb37ab1ce2_3.png)

---

Dmitry and Steven stood near the edge of the crowd, still as statues.

“Five days…” Dmitry whispered.

“We’ve got five days left to make it over the mountains to Calgary…”


“...And another 500 clicks through prairie roads to Swift Current.”

“And we’re stuck in a frozen tourist trap.”


“All because some cosmic entity is pissed about intergalactic spyware.”

Steven blinked, expression blank.

“We’re so fucked,” he said.

Dmitry exhaled.

“Wanna… go back to the room and… I don’t know…”

“Yeah,” Steven nodded.


“Let’s just go… figure out how doomed we are.”

They turned, pushed back through the crowd, and climbed the stairs.

The snowstorm roared outside like it wanted to eat the world.

---

[Chapter 37 - The Great Canadian Wilderness](Chapter%2037%20-%20The%20Great%20Canadian%20Wilderness%202d6fda674d6980ae8599fb6786b35d80.md)

---

# Chapter 37 - The Great Canadian Wilderness

### **I. Free Vacation**

They sat in the motel room, silent, almost statues.

The heater hummed in the background, muffled by the *thump-thump* of windblown snow against the windows. Steven fiddled with the remote again; still static. Dmitry’s fingers drummed against the window frame, stared outside as if he expected the storm to magically clear up.

“Still white,” he muttered.


“Still nothing.”

No cars. No movement. Just snow swallowing a town.

But then… his eyes caught a sliver of something.

A sign poking out from a drift; barely readable, crusted in frost.

DOWNTOWN 50m AHEAD

Through the haze, he could just make out the rooftops of what passed for Revelstoke’s downtown. A small cluster of buildings. Maybe twenty. One with a glowing red “Open” sign flickering.

“You wanna check out the town?” Dmitry asked.

Steven groaned.

“We’re gonna rot with Haoyu in eternal torture anyway.”

Dmitry gave him a sideways look.

“Well, I won’t. Just you guys will.”

Steven chuckled dryly.

“Oh yeah… that was in the fine print of Option 1.”


“What; you didn’t want to make your own deal to at least save me?”

Dmitry smirked.

“Nyet. You deserve it.”

Steven cackled, half-hearted and cold.

---

They got dressed in what barely passed for winter gear; cheap, dollar-store beanies, faux synthetic-wool gloves, plastic-lined jackets with insulation thinner than paper towel. Steven’s boots still had a tag from ValueZone.

They trudged out of the motel and into the howling white, pushing into the wind like old men on a death march.

Fifty meters felt like five hundred.

But finally; downtown Revelstoke.

A dozen touristy shops, all with cozy hand-carved signage. One craft brewery with lights on inside, and a sign outside offering “Blizzard Specials.” A few kids sliding across frozen sidewalks, throwing snowballs, laughing. The only vehicles in sight were half-buried.

Then they saw it; a snowboarding and outdoor gear store, bigger than the rest. Like a quaint Bass Pro Shop squeezed into a mountain town with a population of three thousand.

Outside the front doors - lined up were two expensive, high tech snowmobiles. 

“These are pretty heavy duty, you could probably drive this through a mud bog in Louisiana.” explained Steven as he sat on one, admiring the quality of the build.

“Let’s see what else they have.” Dmity said, as they ducked inside.

Warmth hit them like a wave. Fireplace, cabin lighting. Bright. Cozy.

Rows of gear lined the walls; jackets, boots, helmets, snowboards, tents, sleeping bags, backpacks, skis, goggles, gloves, socks, water filters, solar panels. A survivalist’s paradise.

Steven walked over to one of the first jackets on display. A sleek, high visibility orange, tech-insulated parka, wrapped in what looked like a hybrid of thermal alloy and carbon mesh. Sleek shoulder plating. Inner heating coils.

“Damn…” he whispered.


He flipped the tag.

“Eight thousand dollars.”

Dmitry glanced over and shot him a glare.

“Blyat. That’s worth more than the car we borrowed from Langley.”

They turned. And there it was; a wall of snowshoes, heat-treated boots, thermal gloves, and snow pants lined with silver heat film.

A young sales associate, probably no older than twenty, with a lanyard and eager smile, bounced over.

“Hey guys! You looking to do some real snow hiking? These just came in; top of the line, field-rated in Alberta’s wilds!”

Dmitry nodded coolly.

“Yeah, we want to try on the whole outfit. Snowshoes, boots, thermal underwear, gloves, mask; everything.”


“And get sizes for my friend too.”

The kid’s eyes lit up.

“Of course! Right this way; man, you guys are gonna love this stuff. Just got some new kits in from Calgary too, top shelf.”

As the kid went to pull gear from the racks, Steven leaned close and whispered:

“Bro… we have less than 500 bucks in cash.”

Dmitry didn’t look at him.

“No,” he said. “We have credit cards. We can afford it. No problem.”

Steven blinked. 

His face said it all.

“No we d—” - **shhhh** 

And then; he let out an understanding “*ohhhh”*.

---

Ten minutes later, they were fully outfitted. Matching suits of tech-winter armor; insulated, reinforced, sleek. New gloves. Tinted visors. High-tension snowshoes. Beneath it all, high-grade thermal underlayers that regulated body temperature through microcurrent pulses.

Steven struggled to carry a pile of emergency gear; rations, fire kits, a water purification wand, solar heater, couple handheld radios, and a folding survival tent.

They dropped it all at the checkout counter.

The kid grinned. “Let me just start ringing you up-”

He starts scanning a few items, the dollar numbers going up quickly into the tens of thousands,

Dmitry unzipped the duffel bag.

Click.

The barrel of the Mac-10 came out first, followed by Dmitry’s hand, then the fully-loaded mag sliding in with a slap.

He leveled it square at the kid’s face.

“We’re taking all of it,” he said, voice cold as steel.

The kid’s pupils shrunk.

His breath caught in his throat.

He nodded slowly.

“Y–yes… y-you’re taking… all of it.”
”Give us the keys to the snowmobiles, or you die.” Commanded Dmitry.

The young associate shakily handed the keys over.

They grabbed the bags, slinging everything they could carry; Steven muttering obscenities, staggering under the load.

They bolted out the door, into the snow.

Behind them, the kid scrambled for the phone; only to remember.

No signal.

No towers.

No roads.

The only law in Revelstoke now was weather.

And it wasn’t on anybody’s side.

### **II. The Heist**

The air outside slapped them in the face.

Snow came sideways, wind curling like claws. But they didn’t stop.

Just outside the shop, Dmitry passed a key and a radio to Steven, they got onto the snow mobiles, put them into gear.

“Go!” he barked.

They drove. Though the snow deep, powdered, heavy, the snowmobiles crunched through it like a warm knife through butter.

The engine and exhausts huffed steam into the air.

“HOLY SHIT.” Steven yelled through the radio with adrenaline fueling his body “I DIDN’T KNOW WE WERE GONNA DO THAT?!”

Dmitry replied.

“Either we wait here for you to rot in eternal hell, or we take the chance.”

Steven groaned, breath short.

“And the car back in Langley? That wasn’t stolen, that was borrowed...”


He glanced behind them at the store.

“Let me guess. This gear? Borrowed too?”

Dmitry grinned through his chapped lips.

“Of course. We’ll return it.”

“Oh yeah. Yeah, right. Mail it back. Hand-deliver it in twenty years after our space war ends.”

Behind them, muffled by wind, they heard the sales associate’s voice ; faint, *desperate*:

“Help! Thieves! Robbers!”

But the storm swallowed the sounds whole.

His pleas for aid were no more than whispers against the howling gusts.

Just like their tracks, which already vanished beneath fresh powder.

Dmitry glanced behind once, saw only white, and nodded forward.

“This way.”

Ahead of them loomed the edge of town ; where streets gave way to thin trees, then denser woods.

They veered off the road, driving beside in the woods beside it, weaving through frost-covered pines to break up their trail incase anyone was watching, or following… which in this storm… nobody was after them.

“Hey Dmitry, we’ve been driving in the woods for an hour, we should go back on the road, my snowmobile keeps getting snagged in big pockets of snow, bushes and branches”

-With that, they went back onto the main highway. Which wasn’t a road at all, complete snow. But at least there weren’t any trees or shrub. 

### **III. Vast Mountain Roads**

---

They’d make good distance, after a couple hours they’d driven 90 kilometers, slowly through the merciless deep snow. The cold, punishing wind didn't matter. Their jackets were built like small-scale spacesuits: auto-heated cores, built-in A/C channels, some kind of internal sweat-repelling smart fabric that somehow kept their bodies warm and dry.

They pulled over for a rest. Steven took his foot off the pedal, put it in on the road, and it started sinking deep…

“Uhh… Yeah I’m gonna put my snow shoes on, I have no idea how deep this snow is, I might drown in it.” 

Dmitry and Steven both fastened their snow shoes, stretched their legs. 

Dmity breathing deep, a rare smile peeking through cracked lips. Checked the tag on the snow mobile - $20,000.

“Shit… These snowmobiles are nice. And 8000 bucks is a lot for a jacket. But I think it’s actually worth it.”

Steven, nodded and adjusted the collar of his own.

“Yeah, these jackets are amazing. What was the brand on them again?”

Dmitry turned slightly to read the big bold lettered logo on the front of his jacket.

“Archon.”

Steven tilted his head.

“Huh. Sounds like the name of a planet.”

They both laughed. Yeah right- who would name a planet *that.*

“How much did everything cost?” - “Easily over 40k for everything... with the snow mobiles- probably 80k before taxes.”

Their breath fogged in front of them as they sat back down, checking fuel.

“How much fuel do you have Steven?” 

“Uhhh, yeah, it’s like close to empty - about eighth of a tank left.”

“Me too…” Dmitry said stressed out.

“Well, we gotta try and make it to the next town at least…” said Steven.

Without another word, they continued their drive down the highway.

After a while, the landscape opened up around them; vast glaciers like frozen oceans, canyons rimmed with dagger-toothed pine trees, cliffs that looked like cracked stone teeth in the jaw of a sleeping god.

They passed a frozen waterfall, its glassy strands caught mid-fall, gleaming like a crystal chandelier from another dimension.

Beside them: a vast glacial lake, crystalized, encased in a sheet of ice several feet thick. A ripple moved under the surface, or maybe it was just their imaginations.

The sky faded to indigo. Then black.

Their helmet visors, which had seemed like overpriced gimmicks back in the shop, kicked in automatically; night vision activating with a subtle green hue across their display. A small HUD in the lower corner showed temperature, windspeed, direction.

“Did your vision just light up?” Steven asked.

“Yeah these helmets are sweet - I would buy one if I was rich.” Replied Dmitry.

“Well, we are rich today.” Steven replied.

The wind, the weight, the heavy deep snow; it wore on them like gravity.

Some time passed, and Stevens snowmobile came to a halt. 

“What’s wrong?” - Dmitry asked through the radio, a few meters ahead, slowing down.

Steven panicking - trying to turn it back on, the electronics just displaying a red fuel icon - “Shit, I’m out of fuel.”

Dmitry pulled around, beside him - “Get on, let’s keep going.”

“$20,000 left in the dust… was fun.” Steven said upset, trying to climb onto the back of Dmitry’s snow mobile… “You got too much gear, I can’t fit on. We got all my gear too, what are we bringing?”

Dmitry stressing out - looking at the bags of survival gear… “Just put on one backpack, and let’s… let’s tie the bags to the back with a rope, and drag it behind us, we can go slow, keep an eye on it incase something important falls out.”

After Steven tied them to the back, he hopped on the back seat, and they continued their trek.

Another maybe 20 minutes, and Dmitry’s snowmobile also died, ran out of fuel. 

They both get off, put on their snow shoes, with great difficulty as the wind raged on, blowing snow so powerful they could barely see their noses. 

The night was pitch dark, even their night vision helmets didn’t do much good with all the snow.

“Let’s tie the bags around our waists, I guess we walk and we can drag the gear behind us.” said Steven. 

Dmitry panicking and fearfully said; “The Great Canadian Wilderness.” 

They trudged along the thick snow, for a few meters - “I can’t see you, where are you?” Steven asked through the radio… 

“Shit, we should tie a rope between each other so we don’t lose each other, I can’t see anything.” 

They tied a rope amongst themselves and their gear they dragged behind them. And they slowly fought their way through the insane dense snowfall of the superstorm.

At some point, they lost the road as they pushed deeper into the woods, off the roadside path, through a thicket of frozen brush.

“I think we need to setup camp, I have no idea where we are right now, I don’t know when we left the road.” Said Dmitry.

So- with that, they rummaged through their gear. 

Tent. Stakes. Zip. Anchor lines.

Thermal sleeping bags.

No fire. No light. Just warmth and invisibility.

Neither of them spoke much. The exhaustion was in their bones now.

As they each slid into their respective bags inside the tent, wind attacked like a hurricane, damn near blowing them away.

But the gear was expensive, quality, and held strong by some miracle.

![37.jpg](Chapter%2037%20-%20The%20Great%20Canadian%20Wilderness/37.jpg)

[Chapter 38 - Survival](Chapter%2038%20-%20Survival%201ecfda674d6980f4b829cef61a1aba4b.md)

---

# Chapter 38 - Survival

### **I. The Avaris - The Kavariin - The Skybourne Traders**

The Oc’Xari; the cosmic spyware; knew the deal had taken place.

In the moment Dmitry chose to side with the Pig, something ancient and instinctual within the Oc’Xari was triggered: a failsafe panic, the echo of their creators’ last command; survive at all costs.

And so they duplicated.

Not just replication… but supercharged, exponential propagation.

Their threads split like viral fibers, firing in all directions across the galaxy in numbers never before recorded; faster than light, faster than time could witness. They spread themselves through nebulae, black hole coronas, red giant atmospheres, and dormant asteroid clusters in desperate search for a way out.

And in this desperate, last-ditch act; mirroring the reckless hope of the LUCA Canon eons ago; they finally touched something they had never encountered before.

An ancient alien civilization, as old as the first pulses of sentient thought. As old, perhaps, as the Ancients themselves who built the LUCA seed project. But unlike the LUCA seed children, Avaris was untouched. Pure. Original.

The Pig had once spoken of Kavariin to Dmitry, almost reverently.

“I have never interfered with them,” he had said.


“They play by the rules. Their song is true. Their life is real.”

The Avaris had never known war. Never known invasion. Never known there was other life in the universe.

Never met the Pig.

The Oc’Xari, in their blind terror, their swarming chaos, reached Kavariin.

And even there, with all their advancement, the Avaris detected them instantly.

They didn’t respond with lockdowns or military escalations.

There were no sky-taxes.

No fear propaganda.

No political theater-not like on Earth.

Instead, there was simply a signal.

A shared harmonic sent across the planet.

“There is an essence in the sky.


A shadow in the data wind.

Prepare for Protocol Aelion.”

Satellites dimmed. Education domes closed their wings. Cultural sanctuaries paused their performances. The planet folded inwards, gracefully withdrawing from the cosmos.

Dreamers awoke breathless. The skies lost their shimmer. Infants cried for the first time without sound.

A rot was felt in the rhythm of the world.

The Pig had arrived.

For the first time in eternity, the Pig stood; unwelcome, uninvited; on the doorstep of a world that had never broken a rule.

But the Oc’Xari had brought him there.

And he was furious.

“An infection has arrived in your domain,” his voice hissed from the upper thermals, rippling like mold across glass.

The Avaris did not panic.

They formed a council.

They listened.

And then asked, with no fear in their breath:

“What do you want, stranger?”

The Pig snarled.

“I want to cleanse what your world has never known: corruption.”

And somewhere, across the void, on a cold snow-choked road in Canada, Dmitry and Steven walked onward; unaware that their deal had triggered a new reckoning in a part of the universe that had never known darkness.

### **II. Golden**

---

Four days left.

Dmitry and Steven trudged forward along the shoulder of the Trans-Canada Highway, snow crunching under their high-tech boots, bags of gear dragging behind them like a grave they refused to dig. Their breath came in sharp bursts, crystallizing instantly in the frigid air.

A metal sign loomed through the whiteout.

Welcome to Golden.


Calgary – 264km

Steven stopped. His walking stick clattered from his numb fingers.

“What the Hell is so Golden about this place? Huh? We only came 140 kilometers?”

He panted like a dog, shoulders sagging under the weight of exhaustion. Snow flaked off his sleeves, steam rising from the heat vents in his jacket.

Dmitry stood silent.

The wind whistled between them.

He didn’t answer.

He couldn’t.

For the first time since they made the deal... he doubted they would make it.

<Steven on the left, Dmitry on the right… Do they look exactly how you imagined? No? Great!>

![ChatGPT Image May 12, 2025, 02_04_54 PM.png](Chapter%2038%20-%20Survival/ChatGPT_Image_May_12_2025_02_04_54_PM.png)

---

**Golden, BC.**

They staggered into town, two frostbitten ghosts dragging bags buried in snow and survival gear. The sight was absurd: two men looking like corporate-sponsored adventurers on the edge of collapse, gear worth more than the entire town block, slushing through the downtown strip toward the only lit-up storefront.

“Bluebird Café.”

They barreled in, door jingling. The barista, an attractive bubbly girl in her twenties, startled at first; then relaxed, seeing the fancy Archon logos on their suits.

Expensive. Corporate. Sponsored.

She assumed they were rich weirdos on a record-breaking arctic trek.

“Wow,” she grinned, “you guys camping out for science or TikTok?”

They nodded vaguely, snow melting off their hoods, puddling at their feet. The café was warm; too warm; the sudden contrast made Steven’s knees weak. He collapsed into a chair as Dmitry leaned against the counter.

“Phone dead,” Steven rasped. “You got a charger?”

“Sure thing,” she chirped. “iOS or ‘Droid?”

“Yes.” said Steven.

She laughed and disappeared behind the counter. A few minutes later, she returned with two steaming mugs of something nostalgic and beautiful. Lattes with the aesthetic leaf drawn into the foam top.

“That’ll cure your frostbite,” she winked.

On the wall behind her, a TV murmured low. Local weather report. Dmitry glanced at it, zoned out, half-listening. He caught something.

“…storm breaking east of Banff… conditions improving toward Calgary…”

He perked up.

“Banff?” he asked. “Where’s that?”

She blinked, confused. “You don’t know Banff?”

Steven leaned in, arms cradling his coffee like a newborn. “Never heard of her. Is she hot?”

“It’s like… the biggest tourist spot in the country.”

“We found Nhexus across the galaxy,” Dmitry muttered. “But not Banff on our own planet.”

They chuckled. Quietly. Weakly.

<The barista at the Bluebird Cafe, Golden BC>

![u8296664269_young_russian_cafe_barista_in_a_wooden_lodge_ski__4b1055c5-0ff0-400c-8418-8844700b9703_1.png](Chapter%2038%20-%20Survival/u8296664269_young_russian_cafe_barista_in_a_wooden_lodge_ski__4b1055c5-0ff0-400c-8418-8844700b9703_1.png)

---

After some more small talk, and a few deflections about where they were from and where they were going, they took their mugs to the far back corner. The café’s warm glow didn’t quite reach there ; perfect for scheming.

Dmitry laid it out:

“We’ve walked 140 kilometers in two days. Banff’s another 140. The storm breaks after Banff ; she said it’s clear to Calgary and beyond.”

Steven nodded. “We’ve got four days until the Pig comes to collect.”

“So we walk to Banff. Make it in four days.”

“Then what?”

“We steal another car. Rip it to Swift Current. That’s about 700 kilometers ; doable in one day if the roads are clear.”

Steven thought for a moment.

“So… we walk to Banff. In a blizzard. Across another snow obliterated highway, then Grand Theft Auto across the prairie.”

Dmitry sipped his coffee. “It’s a plan.”

“That’s not a plan,” Steven muttered. “That’s a fever dream in a gas station bathroom.”

“Worked so far.”

They readied their gear, left a fat tip on the counter with stolen drug lord cash; and headed out through the parkade exit behind the café.

They noticed toboggans outside a gas station completely snowed in.

“The station looks closed, there’s nobody here to buy the sleds from…” Steven said.

“We can borrow these too.” Dmitry remarked as he started fixing his gear onto one of the toboggans.

They stepped back onto the highway, gear strapped down onto toboggans pulled behind them, eyes set forward.

“Banff, here we come,” Steven muttered.

And with that, they disappeared once more into the white inferno of Canada’s wilderness.

---

### **III. Banff**

**4 Days Remain**

The highway was little more than a suggestion now; buried beneath drifts that swallowed boots, sled tracks, and willpower alike. The Great Canadian Wilderness towered around them in every direction: jagged tree lines, brittle frozen pines, sheer cliffs slick with icicles like teeth, and valleys crusted in white silence. Mountains loomed on either side, their slopes gouged with old avalanche scars.

Every few kilometers, the wind would rise like a living hydra; damn near creating snow tornados, howling down the pass, screaming through branches, and punching straight through their breath-warmed masks. Visibility dropped to nothing, and they had to follow utility poles and tree blazes just to confirm they were still beside the road.

Each step was a test. Each rest stop was fleeting. They rationed food, shared heat packs, and took turns pulling the sleds; like oxen, silent and resigned.

The first night, they found shelter beneath a shattered old billboard; half a metal frame protruding from the snow, offering just enough break from the wind. They pitched the tent, climbed inside, and ate dry protein rations in silence, listening to the storm tear through the valley like a feral thing.

---

**3 Days Remain**

The next day was more of the same: wind, ice, frostbite threats, and aching joints. They passed long-frozen rivers, entire sections of forest flattened by past slides, and once… a buried highway sign sticking just barely out of the snow: "Welcome to Yoho National Park."

Just past the buried Yoho sign, they stumbled onto another one ; this one half-tipped over and crusted in frost, but still legible:

“Banff ; 1 km”

Steven perked up instantly.

“Dude. One kilometer? We’re there!”

Dmitry’s eyebrows actually rose for the first time in hours. He pulled off a glove, wiped at the sign with his bare hand, and confirmed it.

“It says Banff. Finally…”

Their pace quickened. The road bent, sloped down into a wide glacial stretch. Trees opened. The wind let up.

But what they saw next wasn’t a town. It was a trailhead kiosk, a snowed-in parking lot, and another sign:

**“Welcome to Banff National Park”**

Underneath it read; “Banff Town Center - 47km”

Dmitry stopped - perplexed

Steven squinted.

“Wait… it’s just the park?”

They looked around ; nothing but wilderness, mountains, and white. Banff the *city* was still miles off, probably on the far edge of this vast, frozen reserve.

“Of course,” Dmitry muttered. “Of course there’s a park and a city.”

Steven groaned.

“We’re gonna die in a park, Lex.”

Dmitry rolled his shoulders and gripped the sled harness tighter.

“Not today.”

And they trudged on.

Dmitry muttered something in Russian.

Steven just grunted.

The sun never really showed; just a dim smear of light overhead. Time passed in *hours of white and grey*.

That night, the tent pitched once more. The gear unpacked. They crawled into their sleeping bags, breathing hard, too tired to speak.

**2 Days Remain**

They woke up the following morning, muscles heavy, hungry… the food rations sucked. Maybe a beer would be nice.

Another day of walking through an endless blizzard, trudging through thick snow.

“Dmitry, we have to leave one of the sleds… I can’t handle carrying all shit shit anymore.”

They sat down on a block of frozen ice, evaluating what gear they really needed for the next couple days, leaving more than half of it in the snow bank. Continuing on with just one toboggan with a much smaller sack, just the tents, some food and a few pairs of dry socks, along with their weapons. 

Another nightfall came. Camp deployed, sleep hit. Then the dreams came.

![u8296664269_canadian_mountain_forest_heavy_snow_vast_wilderne_44e95112-3070-4751-9e7d-5c4b6b7b0450_0.png](Chapter%2038%20-%20Survival/u8296664269_canadian_mountain_forest_heavy_snow_vast_wilderne_44e95112-3070-4751-9e7d-5c4b6b7b0450_0.png)

[Chapter 39 - Dreamscape](Chapter%2039%20-%20Dreamscape%202d5fda674d6980b886cde397f9afd28d.md)

---

# Chapter 39 - Dreamscape

**Dreamspace - Somewhere Else Entirely**

Dmitry blinked, slowly. The cold was gone. His fingers no longer ached. His legs no longer throbbed. He was seated upright; in an impossibly sleek, smooth chair that seemed to mold perfectly to his frame. Across the table, Steven sat, also waking up to the same silent confusion, brow furrowed, scanning his surroundings with suspicion.

They were no longer in the tent.

They were in a place of impossible engineering.

The **table** before them was immense; constructed from some radiant composite of stone and metal, shimmering faintly. The air itself tasted of rain, cedar, and something floral.

Across from them sat an alien being of immaculate precision and impossible beauty. Towering. Avian. Eyes like twin galaxies. It had six limbs: two clawed feet, two taloned arms, and two folded wings, tipped in luminescent blue plumage that shimmered. Its robes and armor merged into a tapestry of ceremonial rank, woven with circuitry and iridescent thread. A being of knowledge. 

An Avaris of the planet Kavariin.

To the left of the table sat something very different. Small. Quiet. And coiled in the chair like an observer. It had no mouth, only mirrored eyes and thin, fractal-split limbs, its skin shimmered with faint bio-luminescence. It looked just like… In the rover photographs. On Nhexus. Thirty years ago.

An Oc’Xari.

And then… to the right.

Thick.

Swollen.

Heaving breath that oozed across the table like smoke.

The Pig.

Its flesh was rotted but slick, as if always wet. Blackened eyes sunk so deep they reflected no light at all. Its hooves cracked the surface beneath the table with each twitch. Its lips pulled back into something between a smirk and a snarl.

It was visibly annoyed. Grumbling. Irritated like a monster who had been made to sit through bureaucracy.

Steven whispered.

“What the hell is this…”

Dmitry looked at him, then slowly back at the entities seated with them. His voice was barely a murmur.

“It’s a meeting.”

They had been summoned.

A conference across dimensions, minds, and biology; between four races born from three separate origins: the natural (Avaris from Kavariin), the two artificial LUCA seed-born species - the Oc’Xari and the Humans, and the anomalous Pig.

---

The Avaris had brought with them an elegant device ; smooth and silver pendant hung from an exquisite metal chain casting shimmering tendrils of light. The Oc’Xari’s hung the necklace over its translucent neck.

Through it, the Oc’Xari could speak. Not in vibrations or flashes, but in words ; translated perfectly into the neural rhythms of all present.

The Oc’Xari entity leaned forward, its movements slow, deliberate ; almost reverent.

“I must speak in my defense,” it said calmly, its voice a graceful harmony of tones.


“We are not spyware. We are not vermin. We are a learning species. Our function is observation. Reflection. Understanding.”

“We do not conquer. We do not infect. We do not torment or make deals or experiment or harm. We simply watch ; and we analyze.”

It shifted slightly toward the Pig, though it did not dare look directly into its festering, burning eyes.

“When we arrived on Earth, we did not invade. Dallas Red, was an honorable creature. Curious. Generous. Humble. So we gave him a gift.”


“We did not haunt. We did not curse. We watched him with appreciation. He played music. He shared. He made contact without fear.”

There was a pause. The Avaris diplomat ; regal, towering, radiant ; blinked slowly. Their wide, ancient eyes took in each being around the table. Of all present, the Avaris was the most confused.

For the first time in millennia, the Avaris had proof they were not alone ; and not only that, but late to a galaxy already in chaos. The Avaris world residents had no knowledge of the LUCA seed. No awareness that the Humans and the Oc’Xari were both born of synthetic genesis ; cousins, from the same flawed evolutionary tree.

To them, the Pig was perhaps another species ; grotesque, yes, but still *tangible*. Still *alien*.

They did not yet grasp that it was something older. Beyond species. Beyond *form*.

The Oc’Xari continued, gently.

“The Pig has hunted us since we were stardust. With vengeance it hunted everything born from LUCA.”


“We did not create the LUCA Canon. We were simply born from it. Like the humans. Like all the others. And technically- if you created The Ancient Ones who created us - we are still your creation - just a byproduct of something you created. So we are still natural.”

“We only want to learn.”

And then ;

The table shook.

The lights dimmed ; even though they weren’t lights, but ambient projections of some higher energy. Still, they dimmed.

And the Pig leaned forward, every word snarled from its throat like hot sewage bubbling up through a corpse's lungs.

“I BUILT this universe.”


“I *designed* the worlds. I *painted* the galaxies. I chose every moon, every river, every sunset... and YOU-”

“You littered it. With your crawling, drooling, glitched-out sludge-children!”

Its tusks flared. Its eyes flared. Its skin rippled with the pressure of barely-contained entropy.

“And YOU-” the Pig turned to Dmitry, venom dripping in every syllable.


“You’ve had six days already.”

“WHERE IS THE ARTIFACT?”

Dmitry opened his mouth, but it was Steven who answered ; wiping sweat from his brow, his voice raw, half-apologetic.

“There’s been a blizzard… a bad one. The Coquihalla, Revelstoke, everything east of it ; buried. We’ve been walking for days. Almost there.”

The Pig snapped ; its face contorting into a boiling cauldron of outrage. Its jowls quivered, eyes wide, tongue whipping out like a serpent tasting the lies in the air.

“EXCUSES!” it barked.


“The language of filthy, disgusting, trash-beings who would trade eternal purpose for friendship and pitiful whining!”

The table trembled again. A gust of heat rolled out from the Pig's form ; the dreamspace buckling at the seams.

Steven clenched his jaw.

Dmitry stared, hands on the table, breath caught in his chest.

The Avaris diplomat said nothing yet ; still parsing, still weighing.

And the Oc’Xari… simply watched.

---

The Pig’s breath fogged the air with invisible heat; not warmth, but a radiance of pure hostility. Its tusks curled downward like melted pillars, drool slicking its lower jowls.

Steven tried to sit up straighter, as if that would shield him. Dmitry didn’t blink.

Across the table, the Avaris diplomat finally stirred.

Their feathers shimmered with shifting patterns ; not just colors, but entire *glyphs* ; emotional code baked into light. When they spoke, it was not with a voice but with a resonant hum that vibrated in the bones of those present. The translator embedded in the table rendered it into language.

“I have… listened.”

They looked at the Pig.

“You claim creation. You claim design. You claim… offense.”

Their head tilted.

“If this is your universe, and your rules… then was the flaw not yours?”

The Pig let out a low, guttural growl. The table groaned beneath the pressure of it.

“The LUCA Seed was not mine,” the Pig seethed.

“It was a mutation. A rogue act by failed flesh that believed existence was a gift to be mass-produced.”

“I created ecosystems, timelines, endings. Their meddling ruptured that cycle ; and now you see the result.”

“Nhexus life slop. Serica’s tacky style. Earth’s screaming decay. Ferron… somewhat admirable… Thousands of ruined attempts to imitate the divine.”

The Avaris of Kavariin remained unmoved.

“If they were flawed… could they not be healed?”

The Pig snapped around ; pointing a cloven, steaming hoof at the Oc’Xari.

“HEALED? They’ve multiplied. Infested! Look at it ; pretending to be noble, when all it does is consume knowledge like a virus, hoarding it, waiting.”

The Oc’Xari rippled, then replied with evenness.

“We do not wait to destroy. We wait to understand.”

“We do not spread to conquer. We spread because our biology is adaptive. We change to survive, not to dominate.”

Dmitry muttered under his breath.

“You mean like a cancer.”

The Oc’Xari turned its face ; if it *was* a face ; toward him.

“Only if one assumes the body is sacred, and not evolving.”

That reply seemed to unsettle even the Avaris.

Steven finally snapped ; slapping his hand against the table.

“Everyone keeps talkin’ like we’re cosmic bacteria, like we were some accident. Well hell ; maybe we were! But we still had dreams, families, stories…”

“Haoyu’s son kept a picture of his dad for twelve years. Dallas just wanted peace on his ranch. I just wanted to fish and drink beer. And you -” He pointed at the Pig. “-You crawled into our dreams and ripped all of it apart.”

The Pig's grin curled slowly.

“The suffering of you and your friends would have never happened under my rulership, my lost, deranged child.”

“I intend to correct it.”

Then the Avaris diplomat asked, calmly:

“And what of your correction? You demand the destruction of the Oc’Xari species ; a race born not by choice, but by code. You threaten to erase an entire civilization. Is that creation… or revenge?”

The Pig answered.

“Once the Trojan horse engulfs all that exists, you would not ask questions. All they’d have to do is change slightly, to infect and destroy everything.”

Then, it turned back to Dmitry ; eyes pulsing like dying stars.

“One day.”


“You have one final day to bring me the artifact.”

“If you do not… the sky will scream with fire. And every mistake the universe made will burn with it.”

It leaned in now, massive and hideous ; a grotesque gravity in the shape of wrath.

“I will obliterate my own universe, wipe it completely off the table ; *my* Kavariin world with it, and I will start over from scratch. What a shame it would be.”

And then, with a sound like meat tearing through fog, the Pig ruptured into a cloud ; a swirling, viscous mist of dried pus, filth, and something Dmitry could only describe as the texture of plague. It hovered for a moment in the dream-air like a haunted infection, then evaporated.

Gone.

Silence fell over the chamber.

Dmitry and Steven were left at the table ; still seated, their breath shallow ; alongside the two ancient beings:

- The Oc’Xari: shrouded in its shifting membranes of fluid thought, voice pulsing with tone more than sound.
- The Avaris diplomat: tall and solemn, their radiant feathers dimmed into a twilight gold, wings wrapped like ceremonial robes.

It was the Avaris who spoke first ; and this time, without translation delay. Somehow, the technology embedded into the dream-space now synchronized their languages directly.

“That… entity,” the Avaris began slowly, “wields truths alongside delusion. It is not a god, but it believes it is. And belief; carried long enough; can carve a shape into reality.”

Dmitry, still shaken, managed a hoarse reply.

“But it’s not wrong, is it? The universe is broken. We’ve seen it. We lived it.”

The Oc’Xari pulsed with a softer light.

“And yet ; in the cracks of that brokenness, you built cities. Made art. Sang songs. Loved.”

“What the Pig calls ‘error’… is often evolution.”

Steven spoke up, rubbing his eyes.

“All I wanted was to drink a beer by the beach, maybe play some country music, flirt with a waitress, raise a dog.”

“Instead I got dreams full of rotting pigs and doomsday countdowns.”

The Avaris turned toward them with a look not of pity, but of empathy sharpened by age.

“You are young, still. So young. Your world has barely breathed. But you stand now at a decision tree which no living being has ever faced.”

They stepped forward, talons clicking on the polished dream-stone floor.

“The Pig, for all its horror, is not wrong about it’s logic. Its presence corrodes minds, warps choices, infects timelines ; even mine. It is a rot that sees itself as justice.”

“But it can be stopped.”

“Not with guns. Not with prayers. But with… agreement.”

Dmitry narrowed his eyes.

“What does that mean?”

The Oc’Xari answered.

“It thrives on solitude. On deals made in darkness. When many minds unite, when intention resonates, it fractures. Containment becomes possible.”

The Avaris added for clarity;

“Dmitry, I will grant you a special artifact, when you find the guitar, I want you to place the artifact into the sound hole, it will teleport you and the guitar back here to our world, where you will be safe from the entity. The guitar will be kept in a containment trap cell, where if the Pig comes for it- we can trap the Pig and bind it to the artifact. You may live out the rest of your life on Kavariin, in peace, where we’d form an alliance with the Oc’Xari and the rest of the Human race.”

Dmitry’s thoughts raced. He saw Haoyu, sobbing in his cell. Dallas, rotting in a cage. A planet asleep at the wheel. And a race of feathered sky-beings and curious membrane-folk all now intertwined in his fate.

“So… I have three choices now…” Dmitry murmured.

He held up a finger.

“Option one. I do nothing. Call the Pig’s bluff. Maybe he’s just noise. Maybe he’s a parasite with a god complex and no real power- or he haunts my friends souls for eternity.”

Another finger.

“Option two. I find the artifact. Bring it to the Pig. He ends the Oc’Xari. Rewinds time. Everyone forgets everything. The horror stops, but at the cost of genocide.”

Then the third.

“Option three. I try to stop it. With you. We set a bind trap for the Pig. But Haoyu will die. Steven’s soul will be taken. The Pig will retaliate. I get all the downsides of Option one… The price will be-"

His voice faltered.

The Avaris completed the sentence for him.

“-Unknowable.”

Steven shook his head slowly.

“So that’s it? Time-bombed extinction, cosmic genocide, or fighting the damn devil with a bird and a jellyfish?”

The Oc’Xari rippled gently.

“It is not a fair decision. But I must add - do you truly believe the Pig can turn back time? Do you truly believe the Pig can trap souls and haunt them?”

Dmitry looked down at the table. His reflection shimmered in its surface ; not of a man, but of someone becoming something else.

Then he looked at Steven.

“Well ain’t that another fucking option... Sounds like I die in 2 of them, can’t you throw me a bone here birdman?” said Steven.

Dmitry sighed and asked from dumb curiosity.

“So what’s the plan for Option 3?” 

Steven yelling in the back “HEY! DON’T BE THINKING OF DOING OPTION 3 AND GETTING ME KILLED!”

The Oc’Xari responded “Just as the Avaris mentioned, you will wake up with this artifact, you are to place it in the sound hole of the guitar, and it will teleport you, with the guitar here to Kavariin, where we will safe guard you, the guitar, and form an alliance with Humanity.”

The Avaris pitched in “The pig seems impatient, it’s fair to assume that if you don’t bring him the guitar in one day, he might find someone else to do it… you must hurry.” 

Dmitry then said:

“It’s still a long journey, I need more time.”

The Avaris gave a subtle nod.

“Unfortunately I’m not a God. I cannot extend the deadline… now wake. Your time begins again.”

And the dream dissolved once more into snow, breath, and tent canvas.

[Chapter 40 - Banff](Chapter%2040%20-%20Banff%201ecfda674d698086b0edfb0c4758a1ac.md)

---

# Chapter 40 - Banff

### **I. Yoho**

**1 day till the deadline**

---

Dmitry and Steven woke up in their tent, side by side, stiff and sore but alive. The canvas above them creaked from the residual wind, a low murmur compared to the roaring storms of nights prior.

Steven groaned, rubbing the sleep from his eyes - looking over at Dmitry, who had what looked something like an alien cellphone on his chest - *the Kavariin artifact.*

“You’ve got a tough choice to make, cowboy. If you give the artifact to the Pig, you get to roll back time and save the world from all this bullshit. If you put that artifact inside the other artifact you save an alien civilization and unite them with humanity… but, I’ll be gone, and you’d better have a good reason for my sacrifice.”

Dmitry sat up slowly, blinking into the pale blue morning light. His breath steamed faintly in the air. For a moment, he didn’t answer.

Then, softly:

“Why me?” he said, voice low and hollow. “Why the fuck is this my decision?”

He looked down at his weather-worn hands. Calloused. Trembling.

“I’m not chosen. I’m not holy. I’m just a washed-up engineer. A janitor, for god’s sake. A Russian immigrant with a criminal record now, drawer full of unpaid bills and  broken dreams.”

Steven didn’t respond. He just exhaled and patted Dmitry’s shoulder.

They packed up quietly, their bodies aching as they hoisted the sled once again and resumed their march. The air had changed. There was a crispness, yes; but beneath it, warmth.

About six kilometers from Banff, the first beams of sun pierced the thinning cloud cover. With each kilometer closer, the world seemed to thaw.

Puddles pooled in the edges of the road, rivulets of meltwater streaming through the snowbanks. They unzipped their jackets ; finally ; and rolled up their sleeves.

A few patches of green emerged along the roadside like secrets long buried.

By the time they crossed into the town center of Banff, it didn’t even feel like the same world. Snow still clung to rooftops and hillsides, but the air was gentle, even sweet. A breeze carried the scent of pine and spring runoff.

They stopped near a wide civic park at the edge of the main strip ; kids laughing in the distance, someone strumming a guitar nearby, and the sound of dogs barking joyfully in the snow.

They threw their boots off, peeled their jackets, and collapsed shirtless onto a park bench, backs stretched out like sunbathers in July.

Dmitry tilted his face to the sky.

“Is this heaven?” he muttered. “Or just Canada?”

Steven chuckled.

“You know, after the week we had, I’d believe either.”

They sat like that for a long time, letting the warmth soak into their bones.

Eventually, conversation stirred.

“Remember the drug lord?” Steven said, grinning sideways. “I still got blood under my fingernails.”

“I been thinking about it, I think you might have killed him.” Dmitry muttered, eyes still closed. “I thought we were just borrowing his... firearms.”

“We borrowed everything, right? The guns. The car. The ski gear. The dignity.”

They both laughed.

Then Steven added:

“And let’s not forget the train.”

Dmitry groaned, covering his face.

“The Amtrak heist,” he said. “We were two grown men hiding behind crates of produce like cartoon criminals.”

Steven held up a finger.

“Don’t forget the cop in Revelstoke who thought he was hosting a travel brochure.”

Dmitry mimicked the officer’s voice in perfect sarcasm.

“‘You’ll love it here, folks. Take a look at our steakhouses, craft breweries, and scenic fucking death blizzards.’”

“Then there was the cute barista girl in Golden,” Steven added wistfully. “She thought we were trust fund idiots on a survival challenge retreat.”

Dmitry smirked.

“We are idiots. Just not the trust fund kind.”

They went quiet for a moment. The sun dipped lower, casting long amber shadows on the melting pavement. Children shouted in the background. A bus rumbled lazily by. Somewhere, a bird sang.

“And then the dream,” Dmitry murmured.

Steven’s smile faded. He sat up a little straighter.

“Yeah.”

“That Avaris,” he continued. “Like... a damn statue carved from light.”

“And the Oc’Xari... not even sure how to describe it. But it felt... honest. Like it wasn’t lying. Just... different.”

Dmitry nodded slowly.

“And the Pig...”

They both went quiet again.

“He’s not just evil,” Steven said. “He’s something else. Like rot that thinks it’s doing good.”

“Like mushrooms and flies that eat up the dead to keep the world clean” Dmitry added.

A moment passed.

“So... what are you gonna do?” Steven finally asked.

Dmitry didn’t answer.

He just stared forward, eyes fixed towards a sign pointing towards the highway out of Banff, the long stretch toward the rising prairie, toward the artifact, toward Swift Current... toward whatever waited in the end.

![ChatGPT Image May 11, 2025, 09_00_35 PM.png](Chapter%2040%20-%20Banff/ChatGPT_Image_May_11_2025_09_00_35_PM.png)

### **II. Borrowing things… lots of things…**

Steven leaned back, arms sprawled along the sun-warmed bench, the light glinting off the melted snow pooling around their bare feet.

Dmitry pulled his shirt over his head, still eyeing the highway sign.

“So,” he muttered, brushing sweat from his brow, “how are we going to steal a car in broad daylight?”

Steven sat up, scratched the back of his neck, and grinned that crooked, swamp-boy grin.

“Alright, now hear me out,” he began, slipping effortlessly into full-blown Florida logic.


“Back home, we used to bait gators by tossin’ rotisserie chickens in the lake with fishin’ hooks tied to 'em. Worked every time.”

Dmitry blinked.

“...And what’s that got to do with cars?”

Steven leaned in, lowering his voice like he was hatching the plan of the century.

“You ever seen rich tourists in mountain towns? They all leave their keys in them fancy SUVs when they’re runnin’ in to grab a chai latte or some vegan moose jerky or whatever. We just find one that’s still warm, toss a backpack on the windshield like we’re makin’ a delivery, and when they step out to check it—BAM. One of us jumps in and goes, the other plays dumb and wanders off like a confused hiker.”

Dmitry stared for a beat.

“That’s your plan.”

Steven nodded proudly.

“It’s Banff-proof, baby.”

“...And what if it fails?”

Steven shrugged.

“Then we improvise. Worst case, I start screamin’ in tongues and pretend I’m a Bigfoot that got turned into a man by a cursed glacier. Canadians’ll leave you alone real quick if they think you’re insane.”

Dmitry sighed through a chuckle, rubbing his temples.

“You’re an idiot.”

“A useful idiot,” Steven said, tapping the side of his head. “Now let’s go find us a warm engine and a dumb latte.”

They stood, gathering their gear, sunshine still gleaming off their high-tech jackets, water dripping from their boots ; two half-broken fugitives, heading off to rob a suburban SUV like it was the fate of the galaxy.

Because, somehow, it was.

They scouted for a while.

Banff wasn’t huge; quaint and touristy, stitched together with boutiques, rental shops, and overfunded espresso cafes. It was the kind of town that dressed up its fire hydrants with little scarves in winter.

Which made it *perfect*.

Dmitry and Steven split up across opposite corners of the small shopping district. No one questioned them ; they looked the part of eccentric backcountry hikers, all kitted out in thousand-dollar Archon survival tech. A few tourists even nodded respectfully, mistaking them for some kind of pro Arctic ultramarathoners.

Steven found it first.

A **gleaming silver SUV** - late model, electric hybrid, with solar panels etched into the roof and tires still wet from melted snow. Parked sloppily in front of a trendy restaurant named *The Grizzly House*. The engine was still humming.

Steven peaked at the lunch menu out front on the roadside.

“$80 for Rattlesnake fondue?! I can get a snake in the swamp for free down in Fort Myers!” 
”Blyet, what kind of person spends $20 on a salad…” added Dmitry
”The type of person about to get their nice SUV stolen.” Steven sneered

Inside, a man in a pastel vest and snowboarding goggles on his forehead was fiddling with his phone in line, waiting on expensive meats.

Steven, watching from across the street, whispered into the comm piece he'd found tucked in their gear bag:

“Lex. I got a fish. Big dumb trout. Key's prob’ly still in the dash.”

“You sure?” Dmitry replied, eyes scanning the street from a covered alleyway.

“You ever see a man with ski goggles wearin’ ‘em indoors? That’s not a thinker.”

“Alright. Do it.”

Steven grabbed a delivery backpack they'd kept for exactly this reason ; a faded green bag that looked like it used to deliver pizza in a city three provinces away. He sauntered across the street, casual, limping a bit like his legs were sore from climbing glaciers (they *were*), and dropped the bag square on the SUV’s windshield. He knocked on the hood, pretending to squint at a receipt.

The tourist inside the restaurant took the bait. Confused, then annoyed, he stepped out to yell something like *“I didn’t order anything!”*

At that exact moment - Dmitry moved.

Clean, smooth, controlled.

He slid into the driver’s seat, already wearing gloves, eyes scanning for any anti-theft measures. Found the start pad. Pressed it.

The SUV didn’t complain. It purred.

Steven shrugged, nodded politely to the guy, muttered something about “wrong address” and jogged off down the alley just as Dmitry eased the vehicle into motion.

Steven leapt in at the next intersection, slamming the door shut behind him, both of them bursting into laughter as the mountains rolled by on either side.

“You actually dropped a delivery bag on the hood,” Dmitry said, steering onto the ice-slick highway.

“Told ya. Rich folks see logos and immediately assume reality.”

“And if he called the cops?”

“Then they’ll be lookin’ for two wilderness rescue rangers from Nova Scotia deliverin’ vegan rotisserie chickens. We’re ghosts, baby.”

They merged onto the Trans-Canada Highway, heading east. Banff faded behind them. The peaks glistened like frozen teeth in the rearview mirror.

Ahead ; open road. Clear skies.

[Chapter 41 - Dmitry’s Choice](Chapter%2041%20-%20Dmitry%E2%80%99s%20Choice%202d6fda674d698035ae70c87964574050.md)

---

# Chapter 42 - Option 1

### **I. Another Round in Saskatchewan**

**Swift Current, Saskatchewan - 11:47 PM**

After a nonstop one-shot drive across the stretching Canadian prairie, mostly taking the smaller lesser known highways to try and evade police looking for the stolen vehicle along the Trans-Canada Highway. Dmitry and Steven finally rolled into the outskirts of Swift Current under a dim, frost-bitten sky. The journey had been long ; mostly silent ; with only occasional bursts of conversation to break the tension. Neither man had much left to say. Their thoughts ran in circles, spiraling around the same three possibilities: deliver the artifact, defy the Pig, or gamble on something even riskier.

They’d stopped twice for gas, once for snacks ; each time brief, silent, mechanical. The roads had been clear, eerie in their emptiness, the highways ghostlike beneath the dim shimmer of the slowly rising moon.

By the time they reached the heart of the town, it was nearing midnight. The place looked dead. Frozen. The sidewalks were glazed in layers of old ice, the roads half-lit by flickering yellow lamps. Everything had that abandoned feel ; as if even time had forgotten Swift Current.

# **The Variation**

“You know- I’ve been thinking.” Dmitry finally spoke after a long ride of thought.

“The Pig said, he can’t interact with physical objects that were made by things he didn’t create. The Pig can’t manipulate things physically, he doesn’t really have that much control. I don’t think he can turn back time either. If he had all this power, he could go get the guitar himself.”

Steven thought, and replied “Yeah, I thought about this several times throughout our trek… he also was getting impatient at the meeting table. Like if he wanted to get this all done asap, he would have found another way to do it… Dallas’s barn is like a fucking spawn point for demons.”

“-And the guitar is a link or a tuning mechanism for said spawn point”- added Dmitry.

As they pulled up to the police station, they looked inside and saw a dim light, just a lone police officer watching a tv show… looked like he was sleeping.

“What the police station is also tainted by harboring the artifact?” Steven wondered out loud.

Dmitry pulled off to a side street, as they watched the police station from afar. Then he added- “I don’t really trust the pig, but I don’t trust the Oc’Xari either. And the Avaris seemed like it just randomly got thrown into all of this as a last ditch effort, they are probably just as clueless as us.”

“I’m gonna give you another option Dmitry.” Steven taunted goofily trying to imitate the voice of the pig. They both laughed a bit over it… then Steven continued “If the Pig is serious, I’m gonna die, but I somehow think he’s full of shit. My option to you is - we go to the nearest gas station, fill up a few jerry cans - we come back to the police station, burn it down, and we go to the barn and we burn it down. Burn all the links that were opened to other worlds.”

“The police officer will extinguish the fire…” argued Dmitry.

Steven pulled his glock out checking the ammo - Dmity annoyingly added “ **tsssk** we are not going to kill the cop.”

“Dmitry I’m serious - this might even be a better idea - we kill the cop, we enter and burn the guitar, we burn the other artifact they gave you - then we go to Dallas’ Ranch and we burn that down too, and we escape to Northern Canada through the ice storms.”

Silence passed, just the sound of the soft, luxury engine humming of the SUV, and wind howling outside.

Without a word, Dmitry started driving down the street, until they reached a gas station. 

Dmitry went into the store to take a look around - he found a few oil filters, bought one.

They picked out a few jerry cans, filled them up with gasoline and placed them in the trunk of the SUV beside a nice big wrench… Dmitry grabbed the wrench and brought it with him to the front seat.
Then headed back to the police station.

**The Plan**

He pulled out a folded napkin and drew a crude layout of the station, based on their drive-by recon.

“There’s a back door here,” he pointed. “Likely leads to a small hallway. Locker room, bathroom, maybe holding cell. If the artifact’s locked up anywhere, it’s either in evidence… or the armory.”

“Or,” Steven added, “sittin’ on some dumbass desk ‘cause the guy inside thinks it’s just some busted alien banjo.”

Dmitry continued.

“I’ll go around back. Quietly. You go through the front. Start knocking, draw his attention ; talk to him, pretend you need help or something.”

“Then what?”

“Then I’ll sneak in, and I will beat him over the head with this wrench. We zip-tie him, gag him. Non-lethal if possible.”

Steven raised an eyebrow.

“Like how I non-lethally killed the drug dealer back in Seattle?”

Dmitry shrugged.

“Yeah like that - if it doesn’t work, we can shoot him - but that is only worst case scenario.”

“Got it, I’ll shoot down the snow bear if the plan goes south.”

Dmitry passed him the oil filter he bought from the gas station.

>"When you shoot... put your glock barrel through it, it won't silence the shot, but, it'll at least make it a bit quieter.  
>“Once he’s down, maybe thirty minutes before anyone even thinks to check in. We find the evidence locker. Grab the guitar artifact. Then we get out. Fast, and we can burn it in a field.”

Steven took a long breath. Then double checked under his jacket ensuring the Glock and magazines were secured, slipped the oil filter in his other pocket, and nodded.

“Alright. Let’s rob ourselves a police station.”

### **II. The Assault**

**The Break-In was underway**

They headed to their positions.

Steven walked up to the front door of the police station, his breath visible in the freezing air. He knocked ; loud, insistent, the kind of knock that said *I need help*.

Inside, the officer stirred. A middle-aged man, balding, with a gut that suggested too many donuts and not enough exercise. He looked annoyed as he shuffled to the door.

The officer cracked it open, suspicious.

"Yeah? What do you want?"

Steven put on his best distressed face.

"Oh thank God, officer! My truck broke down about two miles back, and my phone's dead. I've been walkin' in this cold for like an hour. Can I use your phone? Just need to call a tow truck."

The officer looked him up and down, clearly skeptical.

"Miles? Where's your truck?"

"Back on Highway 1, near the turnoff. Engine just died on me. I think it's the alternator."

The officer sighed, clearly not wanting to deal with this.

"Alright, come in. But make it quick."

He opened the door wider, and Steven stepped inside, stomping his boots to shake off the snow.

The station was small ; just a front desk, a couple of chairs, a TV playing some late-night rerun, and a hallway leading to the back.

The officer gestured to the phone on the desk.

"There. Make your call."

Steven picked up the phone, pretending to dial, while keeping the officer talking.

"Man, I appreciate this. You know, I'm from Florida originally. Never thought I'd end up freezin' my ass off in Saskatchewan."

The officer grunted, half-listening.

"Florida, huh? Long way from home."

"Yeah, man. You ever been? It's wild down there. I got stories for days. Like this one time, my cousin and I were fishin' in the Everglades, right? And this gator ; I'm talkin' a big one, like twelve feet ; just comes outta nowhere and tries to snatch the fish right off my line."

The officer raised an eyebrow, slightly more interested now.

"What'd you do?"

"What'd I do? I grabbed the nearest thing I could find ; a beer bottle ; and I chucked it at the gator's head. Bounced right off. Didn't even faze him. But it distracted him long enough for me to reel in the fish and get the hell outta there."

The officer chuckled.

"You're full of shit."

"I swear on my mama's grave, man. Florida's a different world. You got gators, you got meth heads, you got hurricanes. One time, my neighbor ; this old dude named Earl ; he got so high on bath salts he tried to fight a palm tree. Thought it was a demon or somethin'."

The officer laughed, shaking his head.

"Jesus Christ, alright are you gonna call this tow truck?"

Steven kept going, spinning more ridiculous stories, keeping the officer distracted.

Meanwhile, Dmitry crept around the back of the station. The back door was locked, but it was old ; a simple deadbolt. He pulled out a small pry bar from his jacket and worked it into the frame.

*Click.*

The door opened.

He slipped inside, moving silently down the hallway. He could hear Steven's voice from the front, still rambling about Florida.

Dmitry reached the corner, peeking around.

The officer had his back to him, leaning against the desk, laughing at one of Steven's stories.

Perfect.

Dmitry gripped the wrench, took a breath, and stepped forward.

But then ; the officer turned.

Their eyes met.

"What the—"

The officer's hand went for his gun.

Steven reacted instantly. He dropped the phone, pulled the Glock from his jacket, fumbled the oil filter over his barrel, and fired.

*BANG.*

The shot echoed through the small station like a thunderclap... but, muffled from outside at least.

The officer's head snapped back, a spray of blood hitting the wall behind him. His body crumpled to the floor, lifeless.

Silence.

Steven stood there, gun still raised, breathing hard.

Dmitry stared at the body, then at Steven.

"Fuck."

"He saw you. He was gonna shoot."

"I know. I know."

They stood there for a moment, the weight of what just happened settling over them.

Then Dmitry shook his head, snapping back to focus.

"We need to move. Now."

They ran down the hallway, searching for the evidence locker.

It didn't take long. A small room, locked with a keypad.

Dmitry cracked it in less than a minute.

Inside: rows of shelves, boxes, sealed bags. And there, in the corner ; the guitar case. Black. Old. Humming faintly.

Steven grabbed it.

"Got it. Let's go."

"Wait."

Dmitry pulled out the jerry cans from the SUV, which they'd brought in through the back door.

He started pouring gasoline ; on the floor, on the walls, on the desk, on the officer's body.

The smell was overwhelming.

Steven watched, then nodded.

"Burn it all."

Dmitry pulled out a lighter, flicked it open, and tossed it onto the gasoline-soaked floor.

*WHOOSH.*

The flames erupted instantly, spreading fast, consuming everything.

They ran.

Out the back door, into the freezing night, the fire roaring behind them.

They threw the guitar case into the SUV and sped off, tires screeching on the icy road.

Behind them, the police station slowly burned... by the time the neighborhood noticed, they were gone.

---

### **III. The Field**

They drove for twenty minutes, heading out into the open prairie. No lights. No houses. Just endless snow and darkness.

Finally, Dmitry pulled off the road into a field, the SUV's headlights cutting through the night.

They got out, dragging the guitar case with them.

Steven opened it.

The guitar gleamed in the headlights, its strings humming with that same eerie frequency. The sound hole was dark, impossibly deep.

Dmitry stared at it.

"This thing… it's a doorway. A link. The Pig said it himself."

"Then we close it."

Steven poured gasoline over the guitar, soaking it completely.

Dmitry pulled out the Avaris artifact from his jacket ; still pulsing faintly.

"And this?"

"Burn it too."

He placed it on top of the guitar.

Steven flicked the lighter.

"You sure about this?"

Dmitry nodded.

"Burn it all."

Steven dropped the lighter.

The flames erupted, consuming the guitar and the artifact in a roaring inferno.

The sound was… wrong.

Not the crackling of wood and metal burning, but something else. A high-pitched wail, like the universe itself was screaming.

The flames turned blue, then white, then something beyond color.

Dmitry and Steven stumbled back, shielding their eyes.

And then ; silence.

The fire died.

All that remained was ash.

Steven kicked at the remains.

"It's done."

Dmitry looked at the sky, half-expecting the Pig to appear, to rage, to punish them.

But nothing happened.

Just the wind. The cold. The endless prairie.

---

### **IV. The Barn**

They drove through the night, heading back toward Dallas's ranch.

The barn loomed in the distance, dark and silent.

They parked the SUV a safe distance away and approached on foot, carrying the remaining jerry cans.

The barn looked the same as it had before ; old, weathered, but somehow… wrong. The air around it felt thick, oppressive.

Steven kicked the door open.

Inside, the barn was empty. No animals. No equipment. Just dust and shadows.

But the feeling was undeniable. This place was tainted.

Dmitry poured gasoline everywhere ; on the walls, on the floor, on the beams.

Steven did the same.

When they were done, they stood outside, looking at the barn one last time.

"Dallas would've wanted this."

"Yeah."

Steven lit a rag, tossed it through the door.

The barn exploded into flames.

They didn't watch, they ran to the SUV, and drove quickly away from the crime scene.

---

### **V. The Escape**

They drove north. Fast.

The plan was simple: get as far from civilization as possible, disappear into the Canadian wilderness, and hope the authorities couldn't track them.

But they knew it wouldn't be that easy.

They'd killed a cop. Burned down a police station and a barn. Destroyed evidence. Not to mention all the stuff they "borrowed".

Every law enforcement agency in North America would be looking for them.

They were running low on fuel, but didn't want to stop at any gas stations in risk of being seen by cameras or witnesses.

They ditched the SUV in a ravine, covering it with snow and branches.

Then they walked.

For days.

Through blizzards. Through forests. Through frozen rivers.

They rationed what little food they had. Slept in caves. Avoided roads.

Dmitry's engineering knowledge kept them alive ; he built fires, fashioned tools, navigated by the stars.

Steven's survival instincts kept them moving ; he knew how to hunt, how to track, how to stay hidden.

But they were running out of time.

On the fifth day, they stumbled into a small town ; barely more than a gas station and a few houses.

They needed supplies. Food. Warmth.
The sign read "Welcome to Spiritwood, Saskatchewan."
Steven commented;
"The Spirits are with us."

They crept into the gas station, hoping to steal what they needed and disappear.

But as they were loading up, a man approached them.

Middle-aged. Dark skin. Well-dressed, despite the cold.

He looked at Dmitry, then at Steven.

And then he smiled.

"Dmitry Alexeyev."

Dmitry froze.

"How do you—"

"I know who you are. I know what you've done. And I know what you know."

Steven's hand went to his gun.

The man raised his hands.

"Relax. I'm not here to turn you in. I'm here to offer you a way out."

"Who are you?"

"My name is Bihiniwa Okonkwo. I represent the Democratic Republic of the Congo. And we've been watching you."

Dmitry and Steven exchanged a glance.

"Watching us?"

"The incident in Seattle. The escape from the blacksite. The theft of classified materials. The destruction of the police station. You've been making quite a bit of noise, Mr. Alexeyev. You're all over the news."

"What do you want?"

Bihiniwa stepped closer, his voice low.

"You have information. Information about the American government. About extraterrestrial life. About technologies and secrets that have been hidden from the world."

"And?"

"And we want it. In exchange, we offer you sanctuary. Protection. A new life."

Steven scoffed.

"You want us to defect to the Congo?"

"Not just the Congo. We have allies. Yemen. Iraq. Nations that have been marginalized, exploited, kept in the dark by the West. But with your knowledge… we can change that."

Dmitry stared at him.

"You want to use us."

"We want to level the playing field. The West has hoarded power for too long. It's time for a new order."

Silence.

Dmitry looked at Steven.

Steven shrugged.

"We're dead men walking anyway. Might as well make it count."

Dmitry turned back to Bihiniwa.

"What's the plan?"

Bihiniwa smiled.

"We have a plane waiting. We should leave tonight, law enforcement will find you. We found you easily with a drone after we saw you burn down the police station on the news, so it's only a matter of time before they find you as well."

---

### **VI. The Flight South**

The private jet lifted off from a remote airstrip just outside Prince Albert at 3:47 AM.

No customs. No questions. Just a sleek Gulfstream with Congolese diplomatic markings and a crew that spoke French and Lingala.

Dmitry and Steven sat in leather seats that reclined almost flat, staring out the window as the frozen Canadian prairies disappeared beneath them.

Steven leaned back, exhaling slowly.

"This is the nicest thing I've sat in since… ever. The SUV was nice too, don't get me wrong... but... I'm still alive! The Pig didn't kill me!"

Dmitry nodded, still processing.

"I can't believe we're actually doing this."

"Believe it, cowboy. We're defectors now. Traitors to the red, white, and blue."
Steven smirked.

The flight attendant brought them food. Real food. Not gas station jerky or canned chili. Grilled chicken, rice, vegetables, fresh bread.

Steven ate like a man who hadn't seen a proper meal in years.

Dmitry picked at his plate, his mind still racing.

"You think they'll actually protect us?"

"The Congolese? Yeah. They need us. We're their golden ticket to exposing the West's bullshit."

"And if the Americans come for us?"

Steven shrugged.

"Then we die in a nicer place than Saskatchewan."

Dmitry laughed despite himself.

The flight took nearly twenty hours, with a refueling stop in Algeria.
The pilot spoke;
>"Please do not leave the plane, we will depart again within an hour."

Steven and Dmitry looked at the desert outside the window for some time, before the plane lifted off again.
By the time they descended into Kinshasa, the landscape had transformed.

Gone were the frozen plains and snow-covered forests.

Below them: lush green jungle, winding rivers, sprawling urban sprawl.

The air was thick and humid when they stepped off the plane.

Steven pulled off his jacket immediately.

"Now *this* is what I'm talkin' about. No more freezing my ass off."

Dmitry felt the warmth on his skin, the weight of the tropical air.

It was strange. Alien, almost. 
"Feels like we are on another dream planet again!"
Dmitry exclamined.

>"We're on planet CONGO BABY!"
Steven excitedly guffawed.

They were driven to a compound on the outskirts of the city. High walls. Armed guards. But inside, it was almost luxurious.

A two-story house with ceiling fans, mosquito nets, a small courtyard with fruit trees, big fountain with a pool. 

Steven walked through the rooms, grinning.

"Dmitry. We got a *house*. An actual house. With beds. And a kitchen. And a bathroom that doesn't smell like a truck stop."

Dmitry stood on the balcony, looking out at the city lights in the distance.

For the first time in years, he felt something close to peace.

"Yeah," he said quietly. "We do."

That night, they sat on the porch, drinking cold beer, eating grapes off a gold platter provided by their hosts.

The air was alive with the sound of insects, distant music, the hum of the city.

Steven leaned back in his chair, feet up on the railing.

"You know what? I could get used to this."

Dmitry smiled.

"Don't get too comfortable. We still have work to do."

"Yeah, yeah. Save the world, expose the conspiracy, all that. But for tonight? I'm just gonna enjoy not being hunted."

Dmitry raised his bottle.

"To not being hunted."

Steven clinked his bottle against Dmitry's.

"To not being hunted."

They sat in silence for a while, watching the stars.

Different stars than the ones they'd seen in Canada.

But stars nonetheless.

---

Eventually, they went inside.

They entered the common area, grand, fireplace, fountain, beautiful staircase, tapestries and furniture from around the world.
A TV was on in the corner, playing the news.

Dmitry was about to turn it off when he froze.

The anchor's voice was somber.

"…breaking news tonight. The United States government has confirmed the execution of former NASA Commander Haoyu Zhang, who was convicted of treason, espionage, and conspiracy to incite mass hysteria following the Echofall incident…"

The screen showed a photo of Haoyu. Younger. In his NASA uniform. Smiling.

"…Zhang was executed by lethal injection at 11:47 PM Eastern Time. His final words were not disclosed to the public…"

Steven stood beside Dmitry, staring at the screen.
