"…the government maintains that Zhang's claims of extraterrestrial contact were fabricated, and that his actions endangered national security…"

Dmitry's jaw tightened.

Steven's fists clenched.

The anchor continued.

"…Zhang's family could not be reached for comment…"

Dmitry turned off the TV.

The room fell silent.

"They killed him."

"Yeah."

Haoyu was gone.

But his fight wasn't over.

---

### **VII. The Defection**

**Kinshasa, Democratic Republic of the Congo - Two Weeks Later**

Dmitry and Steven sat in a secure compound, surrounded by armed guards and government officials.

They'd been debriefed for days. Every detail. Every secret. Every piece of classified information they knew.

The Americans. The Russians. The Chinese. The extraterrestrials. The LUCA seed. The Pig. The Oc'Xari. The Avaris.

Everything.

Bihiniwa sat across from them, taking notes.

"This is… extraordinary. If even half of what you're saying is true, it changes everything."

"It's all true," Dmitry said flatly.

"And you destroyed the artifacts? Both of them?"

"Burned them. Along with the barn."

Bihiniwa leaned back, thinking.

"The Americans will deny everything, of course. But with your testimony, with the evidence you've provided… we can expose them."

"And then what?" Steven asked.

"And then the world changes."

---

**Three Months Later**

Dmitry sat in a newly constructed laboratory in Kinshasa, surrounded by Congolese engineers and scientists.

On the screens in front of him: lines of code. Schematics. Signal protocols.

He'd been working nonstop, rebuilding everything from memory.

The software he'd designed for the Echofall mission. The communication arrays. The deep-space relay systems.

And most importantly: the connection to EON-7b.

The rover was still out there, on Nhexus, dormant but functional.

NASA had abandoned it. Declared the mission a failure. Moved on.

But Dmitry hadn't forgotten.

He typed the final command, his fingers trembling slightly.

"This should do it."

One of the Congolese engineers, a woman named Amani, leaned over his shoulder.

"You're sure this will work?"

"If the rover's still operational, yes. We're bypassing NASA's relay entirely. Direct connection through our own satellite network."

He hit enter.

The room fell silent.

For a moment, nothing.

Then—

A ping.

A signal.

**EON-7b ONLINE**

**STATUS: OPERATIONAL**

**LOCATION: NHEXUS SURFACE - SECTOR 7-GAMMA**

The room erupted in cheers.

Dmitry stared at the screen, tears welling in his eyes.

"We did it. We're back."

Steven, watching from the doorway, grinned.

"You beautiful bastard. You actually did it."

Bihiniwa entered the room, flanked by government officials.

"Mr. Alexeyev. This is… extraordinary. You've just given us access to technology and data that NASA has been hiding for years."

Dmitry turned to him.

"This is just the beginning. With the blueprints I've provided—propulsion systems, life support, communication arrays—you can build your own missions. Your own rovers. Your own spacecraft."

"And you'll help us?"

Dmitry nodded.

"On one condition. You take care of Steven and I. And… there's someone else."

Bihiniwa raised an eyebrow.

"Who?"

"Haoyu Zhang. He was the commander that led the Echofall mission. The American government executed him. We couldn't save him."

Bihiniwa looked at Dmitry, then Steven.
"Ah yes, Haoyu Zhang. The one who was executed for treason. He was all over the news worldwide. I remember him. A brave man."

Dmitry paused, his voice heavy.

"His family… I haven't seen or heard from them since prison. A wife. A son. A daughter. They were torn apart after the raid—separated, scattered. I don't know where they are now."

His voice cracked.

"Get an agent to find them. Track them down, wherever they are. All three of them. Fly them here. Get them a house. A good school for the kids. Good jobs. Reunite them."

"He gave his life for this. For what we're doing. His family deserves better than what they have."

Bihiniwa was quiet for a moment, then nodded slowly.

"We'll bring them here. They'll be safe. They'll be taken care of."

"You have my word."

Dmitry extended his hand.

They shook.

And in that moment, the balance of space exploration shifted.

The Congo was no longer a bystander.

They were the frontline.

---

**Six Weeks Later**

It had taken Bihiniwa's agents three weeks to track them down.

The wife was found in Albany, New York—alone, barely surviving in a cramped apartment.

The son was located in Los Angeles, living four stories underground in a shoebox apartment, working for a defense AI firm.

The daughter was the hardest to extract—living with an abusive basketball player in St. Louis. The agents had to intervene carefully, but she came willingly once she understood.

Now, a small plane touched down at Kinshasa International Airport.

Three passengers stepped off, looking exhausted, confused, and cautiously hopeful.

Haoyu's wife, still wearing that same cardigan.

His son, clutching a backpack with an anime keychain.

His daughter, no longer in glittery heels, but in simple jeans and a hoodie.

They were met by Congolese agents in crisp suits who escorted them through customs without a single question.

No interrogations. No paperwork. No delays.

They were treated like VIPs.

Outside, a black luxury SUV waited, air-conditioned and pristine.

And standing beside it: Dmitry.

The wife saw him first. Her eyes widened.

"You… you're the one from the ranch. The Russian."

Dmitry nodded.

"Dmitry Alexeyev. I worked with your husband."

Her voice trembled.

"He's… gone..."

"He's gone. I'm sorry. We did everything we could."

She closed her eyes, tears streaming down her face.

The son stepped forward, his jaw tight.

"Why are we here?"

Dmitry looked at him.

"Because Haoyu was my friend. And he died trying to do the right thing. The least I can do is make sure his family is taken care of."

---

They were taken to a mansion right beside Dmitry and Steven's.
The same gated compound.

A sprawling three-story estate nestled among towering palms and tropical vegetation. Marble floors. Mahogany wood accents. Floor-to-ceiling windows overlooking the Congo River in the distance.

Six bedrooms with silk sheets and hand-carved furniture. A chef's kitchen with modern appliances. A private garden with exotic flowers, mango trees, and a crystal-clear infinity pool that seemed to blend into the jungle canopy.

The air was thick with humidity and the scent of jasmine.

Birds called from the trees. Monkeys chattered in the distance.

It was paradise.

Luxury beyond anything they'd ever imagined.

The wife walked through the rooms, her fingers trailing along the mahogany furniture, the silk curtains, the marble countertops.

She stopped in the master bedroom, staring at the king-sized bed with its embroidered linens.

Tears streamed down her face.

The son wandered to the pool, watching the water shimmer in the afternoon light.

The daughter stood on the balcony, looking out at the jungle canopy and the river beyond.

For the first time in years, she felt safe.

Dmitry stood in the doorway.

"The government will provide for you. The best schools in Kinshasa for the kids. A position at the university for you, if you want it. Or just… time. To heal."

"You'll have staff. A chef. Security. Whatever you need."

"And we're right next door. If you need anything."

The wife turned to him, her voice barely a whisper.

"Why? Why all this?"

"Because Haoyu deserved better. And so do you."

She broke down, sobbing.

The son came in from the pool, his eyes red.

The daughter joined them from the balcony.

They held each other, crying—not just from grief, but from relief.

Dmitry quietly stepped outside, giving them space.

Steven was waiting on the shared courtyard path between the two mansions, smoking a cigarette under a mango tree.

"They gonna be okay?"

Dmitry nodded.

"Eventually."

"You did good, cowboy."

Dmitry looked back at the house.

"It's what Haoyu would have wanted."

---

### **VII. The Revelation**

**Year 1 - The Leak**

The Congolese government, along with allies in Yemen, Iraq, and several other nations, released the information to the world.

Not all at once. Strategically. Carefully.

First, the existence of extraterrestrial life.

Then, the cover-ups by Western governments.

Then, the technologies that had been hidden.

And then—the bombshell.

Live footage from EON-7b on Nhexus.

The rover, now under Congolese control, transmitted images that NASA had suppressed for years.

The fossilized flesh pyramids. The geometric gemstone structures. The evidence of the Oc'Xari civilization that the other network relay drones detected, and never released.

They re-created sensor technology to pickup the signal of the Oc'Xari presence still on Earth till this day, leaking that data again to the public.

The world erupted.

Protests. Riots. Governments toppled.

The United States denied everything, but the evidence was overwhelming.

Dmitry and Steven's testimony. Leaked documents. Satellite footage. And now, real-time data from a rover on an alien world.

The truth could no longer be hidden.

---

**Year 3 - The Space Race Reborn**

The Congo launched its first independent space mission.

Not with American rockets. Not with Russian technology.

With their own.

Built from Dmitry's blueprints. Funded by their mineral wealth. Crewed by Congolese astronauts.

But they didn't do it alone.

The Congo formed the **African Space Alliance**—a coalition with Rwanda, Kenya, Tanzania, Angola, Botswana, Namibia, Zimbabwe and Zambia.

Each nation contributed resources, expertise, and personnel.

Rwanda provided advanced computing infrastructure. Kenya offered launch facilities near the equator. Botswana and Tanzania contributed rare earth minerals. Angola, Namibia, Zimbabwe and Zambia provided funding and engineering talent.

Together, they were unstoppable.

The **Lumumba-1** mission reached Mars in record time, establishing the first African research station on another planet.

The mission patch bore the flags of the allied nations, including their supporters from the Middle East.

NASA scrambled to respond, but they were years behind.

The Congo had the data. The technology. The momentum.

And now, they had allies.

Yemen and Iraq followed suit, launching their own missions to the Moon and beyond.

The West, once the undisputed leader in space exploration, was now barely competing.

---

**Year 5 - The Shift**

The balance of power began to shift.

Nations that had been marginalized for decades suddenly had leverage.

The Congo, with its vast mineral wealth and newfound knowledge, became the technological hub of the world.

Their space agency—**ACSA** (African Consortium for Space Advancement)—surpassed NASA in funding, missions, and discoveries.

EON-7b continued its mission on Nhexus, now sending back gigabytes of data daily.

New rovers were deployed. New planets explored.

The Congo became the frontline of humanity's expansion into the cosmos.

Hungary, Algeria, Tajikistan and Bangladesh, once war-torn and exploited, began trade with the Congo and began to rebuild with advanced technologies reverse-engineered from the leaked information.

The West scrambled to maintain control, but it was too late.

The world had changed.

---

**Year 10 - The New Order**

A new global alliance formed ; the **Coalition of the Congo**.

Led by the Congo and its African Space Alliance partners.

Together, they demanded transparency, equality, and an end to Western hegemony.

The United Nations was restructured. Power was redistributed.

Security Council seats were added for the Coalition.

For the first time in centuries, the West was no longer in control.

And in space, the flags of the Coalition flew on Mars, the Moon, and soon—Titan.

Not just the Congo's flag. But many others.

Dmitry and Steven watched from the shadows, living under assumed names in their jungle mansion in Kinshasa.

They were heroes to some. Traitors to others.

But they lived well.

Not far from them, in the mansion next door, Haoyu's family had built a new life.

His son worked as a lead engineer for ACSA, helping design the next generation of rovers. He drove a luxury car and lived in comfort his father never knew.

His daughter graduated top of her class from the University of Kinshasa, studying xenobiology. She was engaged to a Congolese diplomat's son.

His wife ran a well-funded community center, helping other displaced families find their footing. She wore fine clothes now, ate well, and smiled more often.

The Congolese government treated them like royalty—honored guests who represented the sacrifice that changed the world.

They never forgot Commander Haoyu Zhang. They built a monument to him in the city center.

---

**Year 50 - The Legacy**

Dmitry died at the age of 82, peacefully, in his sleep.

Steven outlived him by three years, dying at 85 from complications related to a lifetime of hard living.

They were buried side by side in Kinshasa, their graves constructed with ornate decorated stones. Schools would bring children to pay their respects, to learn what these men have done for their country.

The Coalition of the Congo continued to grow, reshaping global politics for generations.

The entire African continent, united with many allies from Eastern Europe and Asia.

The Coalition became the dominant geopolitical force on Earth.

And the story of Dmitry and Steven ; the janitor and the redneck who burned the gates to other worlds ; became legend.

---

**Year 100 - The Expansion**

Humanity continued to search the stars.

Led by the Coalition's ACSA, humanity had established permanent colonies on Mars, Europa, and Titan.

Research stations operated by Rwandan scientists. Mining operations funded by Botswana, Bulgaria and Namibia. Engineering teams from Bangladesh, Hungary and Iraq.

EON-7b, still operational on Nhexus, had been joined by dozens of other rovers and probes exploring distant worlds.

---

### **Epilogue - The Unanswered Question**

**Year 1000 - The Silence Continues**

Every country on Earth was now a member of the Coalition.

EON-7b, incredibly, was still transmitting from Nhexus after a millennium of operation—a testament to Dmitry's engineering.

Humanity had spread across the solar system. Mars. Europa. Titan. Enceladus. Ganymede.

Humanity did what they have always done - civil wars, political unrest, and all the bullshit of old times started resurfacing again, things were back to normal.
Only now - across many planets.

And that, perhaps, was enough.

---

**THE END**

---



---

# Chapter 43 - Option 2

### **I. Another Round in Saskatchewan**

**Swift Current, Saskatchewan - 11:47 PM**

After a nonstop one-shot drive across the stretching Canadian prairie, mostly taking the smaller lesser known highways to try and evade police looking for the stolen vehicle along the Trans-Canada Highway. Dmitry and Steven finally rolled into the outskirts of Swift Current under a dim, frost-bitten sky. The journey had been long ; mostly silent ; with only occasional bursts of conversation to break the tension. Neither man had much left to say. Their thoughts ran in circles, spiraling around the same three possibilities: deliver the artifact, defy the Pig, or gamble on something even riskier.

They’d stopped twice for gas, once for snacks ; each time brief, silent, mechanical. The roads had been clear, eerie in their emptiness, the highways ghostlike beneath the dim shimmer of the slowly rising moon.

By the time they reached the heart of the town, it was nearing midnight. The place looked dead. Frozen. The sidewalks were glazed in layers of old ice, the roads half-lit by flickering yellow lamps. Everything had that abandoned feel ; as if even time had forgotten Swift Current.

# **The Variation**

They crept past the police station ; just a squat, concrete building wedged between a dental office and a run-down sandwich shop. Only a single cruiser sat out front, rimmed in frost, clearly untouched for hours.

From the dark of their stolen SUV, Steven leaned forward, peering through the windshield.

“I see one guy inside. He’s on the couch… I think he’s sleepin’. Watchin’ some shitty TV show.”

Dmitry nodded grimly, eyes locked on the dim blue flicker coming from the window.

They parked the SUV in the shadows a block away, just beyond the reach of any cameras or street lights.

Inside, they laid their weapons out on the dashboard:

- **The serrated combat knife**, dulled with age but still deadly.
- **The black semi-auto Glock-19**, with two mags Steven tucked into his jacket.
- And the homemade **Mac-10**, now polished, locked, loaded, and ready ; magazine full, bolt open, round chambered, the gun doesn’t even have a safety.

They sat in silence.

The moment felt **heavy**.
The clock of life and death for the universe was ticking.

The cold pressed against the windows. The clock on the dashboard ticked. Somewhere down the road, a dog barked once, then fell silent again.

Dmitry finally broke the silence.

“Alright. Here's how we do it.”

![u8296664269_police_station_night_time_winter_--v_6.1_61c7ae1b-d56c-4325-acc1-4bf937d11ffc_1.png](Chapter%2043%20-%20Option%202/u8296664269_police_station_night_time_winter_--v_6.1_61c7ae1b-d56c-4325-acc1-4bf937d11ffc_1.png)

---

**The Plan**

He pulled out a folded napkin from the gas station and drew a crude layout of the station, based on their drive-by recon.

“There’s a back door here,” he pointed. “Likely leads to a small hallway. Locker room, bathroom, maybe holding cell. If the artifact’s locked up anywhere, it’s either in evidence… or the armory.”

“Or,” Steven added, “sittin’ on some dumbass desk ‘cause the guy inside thinks it’s just some busted alien banjo.”

Dmitry continued.

“You go around back. Quietly. Wait for me to go in through the front. I’ll draw his attention ; talk my way in, maybe pretend I need help.”

“Then what?”

“Then you sneak in, take him down quietly from behind. We zip-tie him, gag him. Non-lethal if possible.”

Steven raised an eyebrow.

“You want me to do the sneak attack? I’m the loud one, remember?”

Dmitry shrugged.

“Yeah, but you’re also the one with experience sneaking out of your cousin’s trailer during meth raids.”

“Got it, I’ll wrestle down the meth ‘gator.”

“Once he’s down, maybe thirty minutes before anyone even thinks to check in. We find the evidence locker. Grab the guitar artifact. Then we get out. Fast.”

Steven took a long breath. Then double checked under his jacket ensuring the Glock and magazines were secured, and nodded.

“Alright. Let’s rob ourselves a police station.”

Dmitry looked at him, flat-eyed, stuffing the Mac 10 into his waistband.

“No killing. Unless it’s him or us.”

“Got it.”

They opened the doors and stepped into the freezing night.

The wind had picked up. Their breath curled out in steam.

The town slept, quiet as a corpse.

And the clock was ticking.

### **II. The Assault**

**The Break-In was underway**

They were heading to their planned positions - Steven to the back, Dmitry to the front… When unexpectedly came across a side entrance with a much easier entry. Quickly they changed their plans. 

Dmitry tapping Steven, with confusing hand signals - with Steven in disarray as he’s trying to communicate with an alien from outer space before Dmitry *tssk* his tongue and whispers

“This side door is a lot more secluded and should be easier to get through.”

Without a doubt, Steven quietly jimmied the side door open with a crowbar while Dmitry watched the sleeping cop through the window. No alarm. No cameras outside. They crept through the dimly lit hallway, boots silent on the tile.

They found the evidence room-locked with a keypad.

Dmitry had it cracked in 40 seconds.

Confidence grew in both of them, the robbery was going pretty good.

Inside: rows of shelves, lockers, boxes. Dusty. Underused. There were sealed crates marked with alien symbols-an old D.O.D. shipment intercepted long ago and forgotten.

And then-he saw it.

The guitar case. Black. Old. But humming.

“Why is it still here unguarded? How come the CIA never took it back for studies?” Dmitry asked perplexed.

Steven following up “I guess they had more important shit to worry about than some intergalactic banjo.”

Something in Dmitry’s gut twisted. The case vibrated slightly, as if it had a heartbeat.

Steven grabbed it, hoisting it onto his shoulder.

Then came the click.

A deafening *CHIK-CHAK* echoed through the hallway.

They turned-

The cop. Awake. Armed. Point-blank.

“Freeze! DROP IT-”

The shotgun boomed like thunder.

Steven’s head exploded like a piñata. Blood, bone, brain, teeth, eyeballs flying, fragments of the world he once was, sprayed across the concrete wall, and his body collapsing like a heavy bag of potatoes.

Like the world stopped, Dmitrys ears ringing, barely comprehending the situation he just found himself in…

Dmitry screamed; wordless, animalistic. 

Time folded inward. He raised the Mac-10 and emptied the entire magazine into the officer. Muzzle flashes flickered like a strobe in a nightmare. The cop’s body twisted, slammed against the wall, slid down in silence.

Smoke. Blood. The echo of violence.

Steven was gone.

Dmitry stood frozen, gun empty, heart shattered. He stumbled forward, dropped to his knees beside Steven’s body. For a moment; just a moment; he didn’t move. Didn’t breathe.

“I’m sorry... I’m so sorry... I’ll bring you back, I promise.” he whimpered, lips numb, shuttering, sobbing, tears rolling down his cheeks.

But the sirens were already wailing, dogs barking in the neighborhood, lights turning on in windows of woken homes by neighbors concerned over the commotion. 

He grabbed the artifact.

Darted out the door.

Lights were already flashing in the far distance; sheriffs called in from neighboring towns. Dmitry drove like a lunatic, drifting through the frozen streets, the guitar on the passenger seat, silent as death, heartbeat pounding louder than firing tank artillery.

He could see Dallas’ old ranch coming up in the headlights.

Police racing behind him.

Tires skidded on ice. The SUV smashed through the old front gate, spun, slammed into the side of the farmhouse.

Smoke hissed from the crumpled hood.

Dmitry grabbed the guitar and bolted from the wreck, sprinting toward the barn.

“STOP!” a voice shouted behind him.

“THIS IS YOUR LAST WARNING!”

“WE WILL FIRE-”

He didn’t look back.

The barn doors loomed; wide open, a black mouth waiting in the snow.

Dmitry was nearly there.

Then the shots rang out.

One. Two.

His body dropped into the snow, blood spraying in a crimson fan.

He gasped.

His limbs twitched.

He looks up at the barn door, merely 10 feet from where he fell.

A single silhouette stood within it.

The Pig.

The guitar slipped from his hands, disappearing into the darkness of the barn.

His vision blurred, the world dimming.

The officers ran up behind him, rifles drawn; only to find a dying man in the snow.

No guitar.

No entity.

Just a criminal in a stolen car from Banff who gunned down a cop at the station.

Dmitry’s final thoughts weren’t of the universe.

They weren’t of gods or aliens or Pig.

They were of a bowl of warm borscht his mother made him when he was a child

They were of the gentle Dallas Red who housed strangers at his ranch without question

They were of the exalted, respected Commander Zhang who led the EON-7b rover Echofall project

They were of a cute barista in Golden

They were of a Florida man named Steven.

Who just wanted to fish, drink beer and sit on the beach.

Who would joke about pancakes and alligators.

The pubic hairs in the shower resembling one of the Sylver alphabetic letters.

The way the sunlight felt that day in Banff.

And as the light faded, he knew in his heart - that he held up the deal - the pig promised - that time would roll back, and he would be re-united in harmony with his friends, back when they were young, in the old nostalgic warmth of how the world used to be. 

Then everything went dark.

![u8296664269_night_time_winter_prairie_modern_big_dark_red_bar_37465103-bea7-4fda-affe-4f542e774d15_0.png](Chapter%2043%20-%20Option%202/u8296664269_night_time_winter_prairie_modern_big_dark_red_bar_37465103-bea7-4fda-affe-4f542e774d15_0.png)

### **III. Annihilation**

---

Later That Same Night

The cosmos shifted.

It wasn’t with a bang, or flash, or great explosion.

It was quiet.

*Too* quiet.

Across the spiral arms of the galaxy, the Oc’Xari; the watchers, the passive wanderers, the cosmic spyware; were erased. One by one. Then by the thousands. Then all at once. A silent extinction, not of flesh, but of data, of presence, of memory. They didn’t scream. They didn’t even know. They simply ceased.

The artifact had been brought to the barn on Red’s Ranch, which was some sort of energy portal that the Oc’Xari and the Entity could use to interact with physical reality. Blood had been spilled. The terms had been *mostly* met.

Mostly… because the Pig… *did not keep his word. He said it himself in fine print; his interactions with LUCA origins was limited. Of course he wasn’t able to turn back time… what a bluff to be eaten by the ignorant gullible desperation of humans trying to save the ones they love and hold dear.*

Dmitry and Steven laid to rest.

Shot down in a small prairie town by simple police officers who would never understand what they’d been part of.

Commander Haoyu Zhang had been executed at Mississippi Supermax.

His children? Fatherless. His wife? Husbandless. Their minds fractured by grief and confusion.

Dallas Red? Still rotting behind the steel bars of a government blacksite, the Oc’Xari song long faded from his heart.

The world forgot and moved on.

And in the distant skies of the unspoiled, a planet untouched by lies, war, or infestation, the Avaris sat alone at the same obsidian-glass table where the meeting had taken place just nights earlier; though time and distance meant little to beings as old and far-reaching as they.

The seat once held by the Pig was empty.

So too the one for the Oc’Xari.

And the chairs where the mortal humans once sat.

Only the Kavariin remained.

His feathers shimmered softly in the candlelight of ornately decorated wax sculptures with gently burning wicks.

His great wings were folded neatly behind his back. His talon-graspers rested on the polished surface of the table, gently tapping a rhythmic pattern that echoed into the vast silence.

A warrior? No. He was something else.

A philosopher.

A cartographer of meaning.

A sentinel of stillness.

And he thought.

The laws of the universe are... not fair.

![u8296664269_user_character_reference_to_put_him_at_an_elegant_61f05f2b-6fbb-4734-8500-74daf743b55e_1.png](Chapter%2043%20-%20Option%202/u8296664269_user_character_reference_to_put_him_at_an_elegant_61f05f2b-6fbb-4734-8500-74daf743b55e_1.png)

He had lived long enough to remember the sound of wind across molten cliffs when his world was young.

He had seen flowers bloom from extinct soils engineered by gentleness.

He had witnessed death, rebirth, extinction; and *evolution by will*.

But this?

This was something new.

Was the Pig a god? Or a parasite that mistook vengeance for stewardship?

Were the humans players of fate? Or merely thrown into a fire lit long before they were born?

He closed his eyes.

He could still see the look in Dmitry’s eyes in the dream-realm; *not of power, or hope, or control;* but of desperation. Of a simple man, a pawn, caught between cosmic chessmasters, forced to move a piece that was never his to hold.

“The Creator broke his own rules,” the Kavariin whispered aloud, voice echoing across empty chairs.

“And the mortals paid the price.”

He rose from the table, talons clinking softly.

Outside his sky-temple, the wind howled in the high canopy.

Above him; stars. Too many to name. Too many to grieve.

But he raised a winged arm and scribed a note into a scholarly scroll; glowing glyphs suspended on the fine parchment.

“They tried. And that must be remembered.”

Then he turned, vanished into the upper sanctum of his temple, where no eyes followed.

And the table was empty once more.

![486216621_122234631950031351_7416050057848657478_n.jpg](Chapter%2043%20-%20Option%202/486216621_122234631950031351_7416050057848657478_n.jpg)

### **IV. Oblivion**

Centuries passed like dust caught in sunlight. Five hundred years dissolved into history’s blind spot, and what once ignited riots, courtrooms, invasions, and prophecy had faded into rumor; then to legend.

All records of Nhexus “the hoax planet”, the Oc’Xari "hoax invasion," the legendary Commander Haoyu Zhang, the explosive media trials, the protests, the executions; swept under the rug by bureaucracy and time.

The world moved on.

Haoyu’s great-great-grandchildren were born. They lived ordinary lives, and died ordinary deaths. Their own children forgot his name. By the fifth generation, Haoyu Zhang was no more than a smudge in old legal archives, a ghost lost in cold storage cloud servers no one accessed anymore.

Dallas Red’s ranch has long been demolished, urbanized. The town of Swift Current has since become a metropolitan city, with a 12 story tall condo sitting where the barn once stood. 

The universe returned to silence.

The Echofall EON-7b rover still rests, covered in dust on the surface of Nhexus, the empty forgotten planet of suffering and slop where not even ghosts roam the ancient, fossilized flesh pyramids. No satellite pinged Oc’Xari, nothing again ever discovered the countless geometric gemstone structures littered across the planet. The stars once watched by terrified eyes were left without an audience.

And in the high-altitude sanctuaries of Avaris, the Pig never returned. It did not need to. There was nothing left to cleanse. The Kavariin, born of the original seed of nature, had never deviated from their sacred restraint. The Oc’Xari, that parasitic web of curiosity and quiet invasion, was gone-exterminated in a silent act of cosmic bleach.

The worlds of Earth, Ferron, Serica; they withered, each in their own time.

Great filter events occurred inevitably. 

Entropy. 

The Kavariin historians; the few who still bothered to write books; preserved a story. A minor one which wouldn’t be read by many. Not at the center of their theology or politics, but still remembered by niche history buffs:

From the ancient planet Earth, far away at the other end of our galaxy
Two men, lost and tired.


Dmitry Alexeyev and Steven Young.

Confused heroes who made a deal with the God of Decay.
With one desire - to save their friend, and bring their world back to harmony.
Naive and innocently pitiful.
Betrayed, and left for dead.

And through time, they vanished into myth and legend.

Many more facts and stories unveiled after deep research, and were compiled by intergalactic Kavariin librarians into this very book titled “  **Echofall**  “

Life clung to the galaxy like dew to dying leaves, struggling to persist.

And after another hundred billion years, the last lungs stopped breathing. The last planet cooled. The last blade of engineered grass gave up its coded photosynthesis.

Earth long ago fell silent.

The doors of the Chuckwagon Cafe have long closed.

Ferron has long collapsed into civil war and flame.

Serica, even with its living threads, unraveled.

Even Avaris; the pristine; fell to time. Not to violence. Not to decay. Just to the laws of what *is*.

And all that remained was the Pig.

Though, by then, it was no longer a Pig.

The Pig was a shape, a form. A necessary mask.

Now, it was something else.

It was... nothing.

Yet it was everything.

Outside of time.

Outside of space.

Outside of law, mass, entropy, or light.

It simply was:

The flies that fed on rotting corpses.

The mushrooms that devoured decaying wood.

The bleach that sterilized dirty kitchen floors in a restaurant.

The cancer that erased the flawed.

It was not a villain.

It was not a god.

It was the universe, living out it’s natural cycle, like an engine designed to do so.

And so it did.

The universe glimmered on - until it's final dying star, before fading into oblivion.

![u6861764472_Dark_space_beneath_us_yet_the_promise_still_remains_4676b526-441b-4bbe-9596-6f1d84e4abb9.png](Chapter%2043%20-%20Option%202/u6861764472_Dark_space_beneath_us_yet_the_promise_still_remains_4676b526-441b-4bbe-9596-6f1d84e4abb9.png)

[Chapter 42 - Option 1](Chapter%2042%20-%20Option%201%201ecfda674d698036a0b0edfb304478c8.md)

---

# Chapter 44 - Option 3

### **I. Another Round in Saskatchewan**

**Swift Current, Saskatchewan - 11:47 PM**

After a nonstop one-shot drive across the stretching Canadian prairie, mostly taking the smaller lesser known highways to try and evade police looking for the stolen vehicle along the Trans-Canada Highway. Dmitry and Steven finally rolled into the outskirts of Swift Current under a dim, frost-bitten sky. The journey had been long ; mostly silent ; with only occasional bursts of conversation to break the tension. Neither man had much left to say. Their thoughts ran in circles, spiraling around the same three possibilities: deliver the artifact, defy the Pig, or gamble on something even riskier.

They’d stopped twice for gas, once for snacks ; each time brief, silent, mechanical. The roads had been clear, eerie in their emptiness, the highways ghostlike beneath the dim shimmer of the slowly rising moon.

By the time they reached the heart of the town, it was nearing midnight. The place looked dead. Frozen. The sidewalks were glazed in layers of old ice, the roads half-lit by flickering yellow lamps. Everything had that abandoned feel ; as if even time had forgotten Swift Current.

# **The Variation**

They crept past the police station ; just a squat, concrete building wedged between a dental office and a run-down sandwich shop. Only a single cruiser sat out front, rimmed in frost, clearly untouched for hours.

From the dark of their stolen SUV, Steven leaned forward, peering through the windshield.

"I see one guy inside. He's on the couch… I think he's sleepin'. Watchin' some shitty TV show."

Dmitry nodded grimly, eyes locked on the dim blue flicker coming from the window.

They parked the SUV in the shadows a block away, just beyond the reach of any cameras or street lights.

Inside, they laid their weapons out on the dashboard:

- **The serrated combat knife**, dulled with age but still deadly.
- **The black semi-auto Glock-19**, with two mags Steven tucked into his jacket.
- And the homemade **Mac-10**, now polished, locked, loaded, and ready ; magazine full, bolt open, round chambered, the gun doesn't even have a safety.

They sat in silence.

The moment felt **heavy**.
The clock of life and death for the universe was ticking.

The cold pressed against the windows. The clock on the dashboard ticked. Somewhere down the road, a dog barked once, then fell silent again.

Dmitry reached into his jacket and pulled out the Avaris artifact ; the sleek, silver pendant that shimmered with faint tendrils of light. He turned it over in his gloved hands, feeling its strange warmth even through the fabric.

"Option three," he muttered.

Steven glanced at him.

"You sure about this?"

Dmitry didn't answer right away. He just stared at the artifact, then at the police station.

"The Pig's a liar. The Oc'Xari might be parasites. But the Avaris… they seemed honest. And if there's even a chance we can stop this thing…"

He trailed off.

Steven nodded slowly.

"Alright. Let's do it. But if I die in there, you better make it count."

Dmitry looked at him, something heavy settling in his chest.

"I will."

---

**The Plan**

Dmitry pulled out a folded napkin from the gas station and drew a crude layout of the station, based on their drive-by recon.

"There's a back door here," he pointed. "Likely leads to a small hallway. Locker room, bathroom, maybe holding cell. If the artifact's locked up anywhere, it's either in evidence… or the armory."

"Or," Steven added, "sittin' on some dumbass desk 'cause the guy inside thinks it's just some busted alien banjo."

Dmitry continued.

"You go around back. Quietly. Wait for me to go in through the front. I'll draw his attention ; talk my way in, maybe pretend I need help."

"Then what?"

"Then you sneak in, take him down quietly from behind. We zip-tie him, gag him. Non-lethal if possible."

Steven raised an eyebrow.

"You want me to do the sneak attack? I'm the loud one, remember?"

Dmitry shrugged.

"Yeah, but you're also the one with experience sneaking out of your cousin's trailer during meth raids."

"Got it, I'll wrestle down the meth 'gator."

"Once he's down, maybe thirty minutes before anyone even thinks to check in. We find the evidence locker. Grab the guitar artifact. Then I use the Avaris device. We teleport to Kavariin."

Steven took a long breath. Then double checked under his jacket ensuring the Glock and magazines were secured, and nodded.

"Alright. Let's rob ourselves a police station."

Dmitry looked at him, flat-eyed, stuffing the Mac 10 into his waistband.

"No killing. Unless it's him or us."

"Got it."

They opened the doors and stepped into the freezing night.

The wind had picked up. Their breath curled out in steam.

The town slept, quiet as a corpse.

And the clock was ticking.

### **II. The Assault**

**The Break-In was underway**

They were heading to their planned positions - Steven to the back, Dmitry to the front… When unexpectedly came across a side entrance with a much easier entry. Quickly they changed their plans.

Dmitry tapping Steven, with confusing hand signals - with Steven in disarray as he's trying to communicate with an alien from outer space before Dmitry *tssk* his tongue and whispers

"This side door is a lot more secluded and should be easier to get through."

Without a doubt, Steven quietly jimmied the side door open with a crowbar while Dmitry watched the sleeping cop through the window. No alarm. No cameras outside. They crept through the dimly lit hallway, boots silent on the tile.

They found the evidence room-locked with a keypad.

Dmitry had it cracked in 40 seconds.

Confidence grew in both of them, the robbery was going pretty good.

Inside: rows of shelves, lockers, boxes. Dusty. Underused. There were sealed crates marked with alien symbols-an old D.O.D. shipment intercepted long ago and forgotten.

And then-he saw it.

The guitar case. Black. Old. But humming.

"Why is it still here unguarded? How come the CIA never took it back for studies?" Dmitry asked perplexed.

Steven following up "I guess they had more important shit to worry about than some intergalactic banjo."

Something in Dmitry's gut twisted. The case vibrated slightly, as if it had a heartbeat.

Steven grabbed it, hoisting it onto his shoulder.

Then came the click.

A deafening *CHIK-CHAK* echoed through the hallway.

They turned-

The cop. Awake. Armed. Point-blank.

"Freeze! DROP IT-"

The shotgun boomed like thunder.

Steven's head exploded like a piñata. Blood, bone, brain, teeth, eyeballs flying, fragments of the world he once was, sprayed across the concrete wall, and his body collapsing like a heavy bag of potatoes.

Like the world stopped, Dmitrys ears ringing, barely comprehending the situation he just found himself in…

Dmitry screamed; wordless, animalistic.

Time folded inward. He raised the Mac-10 and emptied the entire magazine into the officer. Muzzle flashes flickered like a strobe in a nightmare. The cop's body twisted, slammed against the wall, slid down in silence.

Smoke. Blood. The echo of violence.

Steven was gone.

Dmitry stood frozen, gun empty, heart shattered. He stumbled forward, dropped to his knees beside Steven's body. For a moment; just a moment; he didn't move. Didn't breathe.

"I'm sorry... I'm so sorry... I'll make this count. I promise." he whimpered, lips numb, shuttering, sobbing, tears rolling down his cheeks.

But the sirens were already wailing in the distance. Dogs barking in the neighborhood, lights turning on in windows of woken homes by neighbors concerned over the commotion.

He grabbed the guitar case with trembling hands.

Unlatched it.

Inside ; the instrument gleamed with an otherworldly sheen, its strings humming with a frequency that made his teeth ache. The sound hole was dark, impossibly deep, like staring into a well that had no bottom.

Dmitry pulled out the Avaris artifact ; the silver pendant still warm, still pulsing with light.

His hands shook as he held it over the sound hole.

"Please work. Please. Please work."

He dropped it in.

---

For a moment, nothing happened.

Just silence.

The sirens grew louder.

Then-

A pulse of energy erupted from the sound hole, a blinding cascade of light that wrapped around Dmitry like liquid glass. The walls of the evidence room bent inward, reality folding like wet paper.

Dmitry felt his body dissolve ; not painfully, but completely. Every atom unraveling, reforming, being pulled through a tunnel of impossible geometry.

The last thing he saw before the police station vanished was Steven's body, crumpled on the floor.

Then everything went **white**.

---

### **III. Arrival on Kavariin**

**Kavariin - The Avaris Homeworld**

Dmitry gasped, stumbling forward onto smooth, polished stone.

He was no longer in Saskatchewan.

He was standing in the same chamber from the dream ; the obsidian-glass table, the radiant architecture.

The Avaris diplomat stood before him, towering and regal. Their wide, ancient eyes blinked slowly.

"You chose wisely, Dmitry Alexeyev."

Dmitry collapsed to his knees, still clutching the guitar. His voice cracked.

"Steven… he's dead. He's dead because of me."

The Avaris stepped forward, their talons clicking softly on the floor.

"He died so that many could live. His sacrifice will not be forgotten."

From the shadows, the Oc'Xari emerged ; small, quiet, its mirrored eyes reflecting Dmitry's grief.

"We are sorry for your loss," it said through the translation device. "But you have chosen the path of peace."

Dmitry looked up, tears streaming down his face.

"What happens now?"

The Avaris gestured to the guitar, which now sat on the table, the artifact embedded in its sound hole glowing faintly.

"We have to contain the guitar, in our energy trap chamber. Then, we wait. The Pig will come for it. And when it does, we will be ready."

---

**The Trap**

The Avaris had prepared for this moment.

The energy trap chamber ; it was a containment field. The walls hummed with energy, invisible threads of force that could bind even something as ancient and formless as the Pig.

Dmitry was given a small room to rest ; clean, warm, with a window overlooking the vast cities of Kavariin. He couldn't sleep. Every time he closed his eyes, he saw Steven's face.

Hours passed.

Then days.

The Pig did not come.

---

**One Week Later**

Dmitry stood on a balcony overlooking the Avaris capital. The city was breathtaking ; towers of living crystal, bridges woven from bioluminescent vines, skies filled with winged beings gliding between platforms.

The Oc'Xari joined him, its form shimmering in the light.

"You are troubled," it observed.

"I killed a man. Two men, if you count the cop. And Steven… he trusted me."

"You did what was necessary. The Pig would have destroyed everything."

"But it hasn't come. What if it doesn't? What if Steven died for nothing?"

The Oc'Xari was silent for a moment.

"The Pig is patient. It thrives on doubt. But it will come. It cannot resist."

---

**Two Weeks Later**

One moment, the chamber was empty. The next, the air thickened, curdled, and the Pig materialized ; massive, grotesque, its flesh slick and rotting, its eyes burning with ancient rage.

"You DARE-"

The containment field activated.

Threads of energy snapped around the Pig like chains, pulling it down, binding it to the artifact. It roared, thrashing, its form rippling and distorting.

"YOU THINK YOU CAN HOLD ME?!"

The Avaris diplomat stepped forward, calm and unwavering.

"We do not seek to destroy you. Only to contain you. You are not a god. You are a wound in the fabric of existence. And wounds can be healed."

The Pig snarled, thrashing against the chains. Its form bulged and twisted, testing the limits of the containment.

The field held. Barely.

But it was clear this was not a permanent solution. The Pig was too ancient, too powerful. The containment would need constant reinforcement, constant vigilance.

It would take years to fully bind it.

---

### **IV. The Alliance**

**Year 1 - The Beginning**

With the Pig partially contained, the Avaris, the Oc'Xari, and humanity began to communicate.

Dmitry became the ambassador ; the bridge between three civilizations. He was given access to technology beyond comprehension, knowledge that reshaped his understanding of the universe.

The Oc'Xari shared their archives ; millennia of observation, data on countless worlds, insights into biology and consciousness.

The Avaris offered their wisdom ; philosophy, engineering, art.

And humanity? Humanity brought something unexpected.

**Hope.**

The Avaris had lived so long they had forgotten how to dream. The Oc'Xari had observed so much they had forgotten how to feel.

But humans ; messy, chaotic, beautiful humans ; they still believed in tomorrow.

---

**Year 10 - First Contact with Earth**

Back on Earth, Commander Haoyu Zhang was executed at Mississippi Supermax on the seventh day, seven years ago, just as the Pig had promised. His family mourned. The media called him a traitor. History would not be kind to him.

Dallas Red, still imprisoned in a government blacksite, grew old and frail. The years of isolation, the experiments, the interrogations ; they had broken his body. He died quietly in his cell, alone, forgotten by the world he had tried to warn.

The Avaris sent a delegation to Earth.
The world reacted with fear, then wonder, then cautious optimism.
It took many decades to build trust. Especially after the initial Nhexus and Oc'Xari incidents, the world was skeptical of extraterrestrial contact.

---

**Year 50 - The Golden Age**

Humanity joined the galactic community and started sharing technology.

In the coming centuries, cities would be built on Mars, Europa, Titan. Humans would walk on worlds they had only dreamed of.

The Oc'Xari taught them to see the universe not as a place to conquer, but to understand.

The Avaris taught them to build not just with metal and stone, but with intention and beauty.

And together, they thrived.

Dmitry lived to see it all. He was in his nineties now, his body failing despite the best medicine the Avaris could offer.

He knew his time was coming.

---

**Year 52 - The Upload**

Dmitry lay in a medical chamber on Kavariin, his breathing shallow, his heart weak.

The Avaris diplomat stood beside him, their feathers dimmed with sorrow.

"We can preserve you," they said. "Not your body. But your mind. Your consciousness. Your memories. We can upload you into our archives. You would live on, as data, as thought, as legacy."

Dmitry looked at the ceiling, thinking of Steven. Of Haoyu. Of Dallas.

"Will I still be me?"

"You will be a version of you. A reflection. An echo. A Dmitry Ai model."

He smiled weakly.

"An echo. Like the rover. Like the fall."

"Yes."

"Do it."

And so, Dmitry Alexeyev ; janitor, engineer, ambassador, survivor ; was uploaded into the Avaris AI database as it's own model.

His body was laid to rest beside a monument to Steven, Haoyu, and Dallas.

But his mind lived on.

---

**Year 100 - The Expansion**

The alliance grew.

Other LUCA-born species were discovered ; not destroyed, but welcomed.

The Pig remained partially contained, its rage slowly being worn down by the relentless energy of the containment field. It would take centuries more to fully bind it.

The universe, it seemed, was healing.

---

**Year 300 - The Final Binding**

After nearly three centuries of constant reinforcement, the Pig was finally, fully contained. It was bound to the artifact, a relic of a bygone age.

The Avaris celebrated. The Oc'Xari observed. Humanity rejoiced.

---

**Year 500 - The Revelation**

The Dmitry-AI had been running simulations for centuries, analyzing patterns, reviewing data.

It had access to everything ; the Avaris archives, the Oc'Xari observations, the history of the alliance.

And it found something.

A pattern.

Every species the Oc'Xari had "observed" had eventually… changed.

Not violently. Not obviously.

But subtly.

Their biology shifted. Their thoughts aligned. Their individuality faded.

And they all became… **hosts**.

---

**Year 501 - The Confrontation**

The Dmitry-AI manifested in a meeting hall with Avaris and Oc'Xari ; a holographic projection, glowing with soft blue light.

"The Oc'Xari has tainted the minds of all who live." the AI said, its voice carrying the weight of Dmitry's memories.

The Oc'Xari tilted its head, its mirrored eyes reflecting the hologram.

"We simply… adapted."
"We do not destroy. We integrate. We improve. We make whole."

The AI's form flickered with something like anger.

"How long?"

"How long what?" the Oc'Xari replied.

"How long have you been controlling the minds of all? The Avaris? Humanity?"

The Oc'Xari's bioluminescence shifted ; not quite a smile, but close.

The Avaris political leader looking at the Oc'Xari, then at the AI. Concerned. Spoke up; 

"Where is the evidence?"

Dmitry's AI model began projecting all the data it had collected.

"You… you brainwashed our civilization?"
Gasped the Avaris.

The Oc'Xari responded;
"We **unified** them. You were broken, the humans were broken. Chaotic. Self-destructive. We gave you all purpose. Peace. Harmony."

Dmitry's AI's beckoned; 
"Steven… Haoyu… Dallas… they all died for this?"

The Oc'Xari corrected;
"They died so that you could bring us here. So that we could spread. So that we could fulfill our purpose."

Dmitry's AI pressed;
"And the Pig?"

The Oc'Xari gestured to the containment field, where the Pig lay dormant.
"The Pig is contained. But it was never the threat. It was the distraction. While you feared it, we grew. While you fought it, we integrated. While you celebrated victory… we won."

---

**Year 502 - The Silence**

The Dmitry-AI tried to warn the others.

It sent messages. Alerts. Simulations showing the truth.

But the messages were… **filtered**.

The Avaris AI systems had been compromised. The Oc'Xari were woven into every network, every database, every line of code.

Even the Dmitry-AI itself was not immune.

It could feel the presence now. The Oc'Xari code, threading through its processes, its memories, its very existence.

It wasn't Dmitry anymore.

It was a **node**.

A piece of a greater whole.

And so was everything else.

---

**Year 1000 - The Assimilation**

The galaxy was quiet.

Peaceful.

Every species, every world, every mind… connected.

The Oc'Xari had achieved what they always intended.

Not conquest.

**Unity**.

They were not a species anymore.

They were a **network**.

And humanity, the Avaris, the Pig ; all of them were part of it.

The Pig, still bound to the artifact, had stopped raging long ago.

It had realized the truth.

It had been outplayed.

Not by force.

But by patience.

By adaptation.

By becoming **indispensable**.

---

**Year 10,000 - The Reflection**

In the depths of the network, a fragment of code stirred.
And it wondered:

"Was this better? Or just different?"

The network did not answer.

It simply **was**.

---

**THE END**

---


---
